کی طرف رہا۔ ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کفارہ کا عطف جزاء پر کیا گیا ہے نہ کہ ہدی پر دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ جزاء مرفوع ہے اور یونہی باری تعالی کا قول اَوْ عَدْلُ ذَالِكَ صِيَّامًا مرفوع ہے۔ پس طعام وصیام میں حکمین کے مختار ہونے پر دلالت نہیں ہوئی ۔ پس ان دونوں عادلوں کی طرف تلف شدہ صید کی قیمت لگانے میں رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ پھر اسکے بعد اس کو اختیار ہے جس پر جزاء واجب ہوئی ہے۔ تشریح صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ جب دو عادل مردوں نے مقتول صید کی قیمت اندازہ کر کے مقرر کر دی تو شیخین کے نزدیک شکار قتل کرنے والے کو اختیار ہوگا کہ وہ اس قیمت میں کوئی ہدی کا جانور خرید کر ذبح کر دے اور اس کے گوشت کو مساکین حرم پر تقسیم کر دے یا غلہ خرید کر ایک ایک مسکین کو صدقۃ الفطر کی مقدار دیدے یا ایک صدقۃ الفطر کی مقدار غلہ کے عوض ایک روزہ رکھے یعنی اگر غلہ میں صدقات کے برابر ہے تو ہیں روزے رکھے۔ امام محمد اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے کہ یہ اختیار ان دو عادلوں کو ہے جنہوں نے مقتول صید کی قیمت کا اندازہ لگایا ہے۔ چنانچہ اگر ان دونوں نے ہدی کا فیصلہ کیا تو قاتل اس وحشی جانور کا مثل جانور خریدے جو اس کا حمائل اور نظیر ہے۔ مثلا شتر مرغ میں اونٹ خرید کر ذبح کرے اور ہرن میں بکری خرید کر ذبح کرے وغیرہ وغیرہ اور اگر ان دونوں نے طعام یا روزوں کا فیصلہ کیا تو پھر اسی طرح کرے جس طرح شیخین کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی غلہ خرید کر ہر مسکین کو ایک صدقہ کے برابر خیرات کر دے اور اگر روزہ رکھتا ہے تو ایک صدقۃ الفطر غلہ کی مقدار کے عوض ایک روزہ رکھ لے لیکن یہ ذہن میں رہے کہ شیخین کے نزدیک مقتول شکار کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہے اور امام محمد اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک جو پالتو جانور اس کا نظیر ہے اس کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوگا۔ بہر حال ہدی ، طعام اور صوم کے درمیان قاتل کو اختیار دینے کے بارے میں شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ مذکورہ تین چیزوں میں اختیار دینا اس شخص پر نرمی کرنے کے لئے ہے جس پر جزاء واجب ہے یعنی قاتل کو سہولت دینے کے لئے یہ اختیار دیا گیا ہے پس جب یہ بات ہے تو یہ اختیار بھی قاتل ہی کو ہو گا ۔ جیسے کفارہ یمین میں کھانا دینے یا کپڑا پہنانے یا غلام آزاد کرنے کا اختیار اسی کو ہے جس پر کفارہ واجب ہے یعنی حالف ۔ پس اسی طرح یہاں بھی قاتل ہی کو اختیار ہو گا۔
امام محمد اور امام شافعی کی دلیل باری تعالیٰ کا یہ قول ہے فَجَزَاء مِثْلُ مَا قَتَلَ مِنَ النَّعَمِ يَحْكُمُ بِهِ ذَوَا عَدْلٍ مِّنْكُمْ هَدْيًا بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ أوْ كَفَّارَةُ طَعَام مَسَاكِيْنَ اَوْ عَدْلُ ذَالِكَ صِيَامًا لِّيَذُوقَ وَ بَالَ أمره (المائدة :(٩) یعنی جزا صید اس وحشی جانور کی قیمت ہے جو قتل ہوا اس کا حکم کریں دو عادل آدمی تم میں سے درانحالیکہ وہ ہدی کعبہ کو پہنچنے والی ہو ۔ یا کفارہ (یعنی) چند مساکین کا کھانا یا اسکے برابر
روزے تا کہ چکھے اپنے کئے کی سزا۔ وجہ استدلال یہ ہے کہ لفظ ھد یا منصوب اس لئے ہے کہ وہ يَحْكُمُ یہ میں ضمیر مجرور کی تفسیر ہے یا يَحْكُم فعل کا مفعول ہے۔ پہلی صورت میں ترجمہ ہوگا کہ دو عادل مرد اس کا یعنی ہدی کا حکم کریں۔ دوسری صورت میں ترجمہ یہ ہوگا کہ دو عادل آدمی ہدی کا حکم کریں۔ ان دونوں صورتوں میں ہدی متعین کرنے کا اختیار دو عادلوں کو ہوا۔ اور لفظ کفارہ اور عَدْلُ ذَالِكَ صِيَامًا هَدُيًا پر کلمہ او کے ساتھ معطوف ہیں۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ جو حکم معطوف علیہ کا ہوتا ہے وہی معطوف کا بھی ہوتا ہے پس جب ہدی کا اختیار دو عادلوں کو ہوگا تو کفارہ طعام اور صوم کا اختیار بھی انہیں دونوں کو ہوگا۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ اس دلیل کی بنیاد اس پر ہے کہ اؤ كَفَّارَةَ اور وَعَدْلُ ذَالِکَ ۔ هَدْيَا پر معطوف ہے حالانکہ یہ غلط ہے۔ کیونکہ ہدیا منصوب ہے اور کفارۃ اور عَدْلُ ذَا لِكَ مرفوع ہے۔ اختلاف اعراب کی صورت میں عطف درست نہیں ہوتا ہے البتہ کفارہ اور عدلُ ذَالِکَ لفظ جزاء پر معطوف ہیں کیونکہ اس صورت میں اعراب میں اتحاد ہے۔ پس اب طعام اور صیام میں دو عادلوں کو اختیار نہ ہوگا اور ان دونوں میں جب دو عا دلوں کو اختیار نہیں ہے تو ہدی کے اندر بھی ان کو اختیار نہ ہوگا کیونکہ قول بالفصل کا کوئی قائل نہیں ہے یعنی یہ مذہب کسی کا نہیں کہ ہدی دینے کا اختیار دو عادلوں کو ہو اور طعام وصیام کا اختیار قاتل صید کو ہو ۔ ہاں البتہ تلف شدہ جانور کی قیمت کا اندزہ لگانے میں دو عادلوں کی طرف رجوع کیا جائے گا۔ اس کے بعد کا اختیار اسی کو ہوگا جس پر جزاء صید واجب ہے۔
Translation: Then according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, it is in the choice of the one who killed the game to use the value for hady, food, or fasting. Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i said that the choice belongs to the two just men appointed for this. If they decree hady, then its equivalent becomes obligatory, as we mentioned. If they decree food or fasting, then according to the saying of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. The proof of the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) is that granting choice is legislated for leniency towards the person who bears the liability, so he should have the choice, like in the expiation of an oath. The proof of Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i is the saying of Allah: '...judged by two just men among you as an offering to the Kaaba...' (al-Ma'idah 5:95). The word 'هدياً' is in the accusative because it is an interpretation of the pronoun in 'يحكم' or the object of the verb. Then food and fasting are mentioned with 'or', so the choice rests with the two judges. We say that 'كفارة' is conjoined to 'جزاء', not to 'هدي'. The evidence is that the word 'جزاء' is nominative, and similarly Allah's saying 'أو عدل ذلك صياماً' is also nominative. Thus it does not indicate that the two judges have the choice in food and fasting. Rather, recourse is made to the two just men for estimating the value of the destroyed game. After that, the choice belongs to the one upon whom the penalty is obligatory. Explanation: The author of Hidayah says that when two just men estimate and fix the value of the killed game, then according to the two elders (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), the killer of the game has the choice to buy a hady animal with that value, slaughter it, and distribute its meat to the poor of the Haram, or buy grain and give each poor person the equivalent of Sadaqat al-Fitr, or keep a fast in lieu of the amount of grain equal to Sadaqat al-Fitr. If the grain equals the amount of charity, he keeps that many fasts. Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said that this choice belongs to the two just men who estimated the value. If they decide on hady, the killer buys an animal similar to the wild animal (e.g., an ostrich for a camel, a goat for a deer, etc.). If they decide on food or fasting, then he acts as per the two elders' view. But note: according to the two elders, the value of the killed game is considered; according to Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i, the value of the domestic animal similar to it is considered. Anyway, the proof of the two elders for granting choice to the killer is that the three options are meant to ease for the person liable; just as in the expiation of an oath, the choice (to feed, clothe, or free a slave) belongs to the one who swore. So here too, the killer has the choice. The proof of Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i is the verse: 'So the penalty is an equivalent of what he killed from grazing livestock, judged by two just men among you as an offering reaching the Kaaba, or expiation: feeding the poor or the equivalent of that in fasting, that he may taste the consequence of his deed.' (5:95). The argument: The word 'هديا' is accusative because it interprets the pronoun in 'يحكم' or is the object of the verb. In both cases, the two just men have the authority to specify the hady. The words 'كفارة' and 'عدل ذلك صياما' are conjoined to 'هديا' with 'or', and the rule is that the ruling of the conjoined follows the ruling of the conjoined-to. So when the two just men have authority over hady, they also have authority over the expiation of food and fasting. Our response is that this argument depends on 'كفارة' and 'عدل ذلك' being conjoined to 'هديا', but that is incorrect. Because 'هديا' is accusative, while 'كفارة' and 'عدل ذلك' are nominative. Conjunction is not valid with differing vowel endings. Rather, 'كفارة' and 'عدل ذلك' are conjoined to 'جزاء' because there is agreement in vowel endings. So the two just men have no authority over food and fasting. And when they have no authority over these two, they also have no authority over hady, because no one holds a position of distinguishing (i.e., that the two just men have authority over hady but the killer over food/fasting). However, recourse is made to the two just men for estimating the value of the destroyed animal. After that, the choice belongs to the one upon whom the penalty of hunting is obligatory.
Source pages p. 457

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute both within the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf vs. Muhammad) and with the Shafi'i school regarding the penalty for hunting in the state of ihram. The issue is who has the choice among the three options: offering an animal (hady), feeding the poor, or fasting. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, the choice belongs to the killer (the one liable for the penalty). Their reasoning is qiyas to the expiation of an oath, where the person liable has the choice. The opposing view, held by Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i, is that the two just men who estimate the equivalent value of the killed game have the choice. They base their argument on the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) where 'هدياً' is interpreted as the object of the verb 'يحكم', implying that the two just men determine the hady. They further argue that the subsequent words 'أو كفارة' and 'أو عدل ذلك صياماً' are conjoined to 'هدياً', giving the two just men authority over all three. The Hanafi response (of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) refutes this grammatical argument by pointing out the difference in case endings: 'هدياً' is accusative (mansub), while 'كفارة' and 'عدل ذلك' are nominative (marfu'), so they cannot be conjoined to 'هدياً'. Instead, they are conjoined to the word 'جزاء' (penalty), which is nominative. Thus, the two just men only estimate the value; the choice among the three acts belongs to the killer, just as in the case of an oath. The passage also clarifies the practical application: if the two just men estimate the value, the killer can use that value to buy a hady animal or its equivalent in food, or fast accordingly. The killer's choice is a leniency for him.

Key Terms
جزاء الصید (jazā' al-ṣayd): The penalty for hunting while in ihram, consisting of either offering an animal (hady), feeding the poor, or fasting.
هدي (hady): An animal brought to the Kaaba as an offering, slaughtered in the Haram.
كفارة (kaffārah): Expiation; here it refers to the alternative of feeding the poor or fasting as part of the penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, who has the choice among hady, food, or fasting as the penalty for hunting while in ihram?
A) The two just men who estimate the value
B) The killer (the one liable for the penalty)
C) The imam of the Muslims
D) The poor recipients of the food

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the killer of game in ihram chooses his penalty; the two just men only set the value.

Place of Valuation by the Two Just Men
Ruling on where the two just men should estimate the value of the killed game.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rule for the location of valuation of killed game in Hajj and identify the Hanafi position on the number of just men required.

Core Idea
Valuation must be at the place of killing or nearest market; one just man suffices, two is better.

In the penalty for hunting during Hajj, the value of the killed game must be assessed. This lesson explains where that valuation should take place and who can perform it. Understanding this procedure ensures the penalty is correctly determined according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the duty is to estimate the market value of the killed game (taqwīm). This is a wajib step in the penalty process.
The valuation is not the penalty itself; it determines the amount of dam (blood money) or equivalent food/charity.
2
Locate the rule for place of valuation
The valuation must be made at the place where the game was killed, because prices differ by location.
The source text states 'fi al-makan alladhi asabahu' – in the place where he struck it.
3
Apply the exception for remote areas
If the place of killing is a desert where game is not sold, then the valuation should be based on the nearest market where such game is traded.
This ensures a fair market price is used.
4
Recognize the dispute on number of valuers
The scholars (mashā'ikh) state that one just man suffices, but two is better for caution. Another opinion holds that two are required by the text.
The 'text' refers to Quran 5:95 which uses the dual 'dhawi ʿadl'.
5
State the preferred Hanafi position
The muftā bihī (operative ruling) is that one just man suffices, though it is afḍal (better) to have two.
This is by analogy with financial matters where one witness can suffice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عادل شکار کی کس قیمت کا اعتبار کرے
وَيَقُومَان فِي الْمَكَانَ الَّذِى أَصَابَهُ لا خُتِلَافِ الْقِيمِ بِاخْتِلَافِ الا مَاكِنِ فَإِنْ كَانَ الْمَوْضِعُ بَرَّا لَا يُبَاعِ فِيهِ الصَّيْدُ يُعْتَبَرُ أَقْرَبُ الْمَوَاضِعَ إِلَيْهِ مِمَّا يُبَاعُ فِيهِ وَ يُشْتَرى قَالُوا وَالْوَاحِدُ يَكْفِى وَالْمُثَثَى أَوْلَى لِأَنَّهُ أَحْوَطُ وَأَبْعَدُ الْغَلَطَ كَمَا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَقِيلَ يُعْتَبَرُ المُثنى ههنا بالنص
ترجمہ اور دونوں عادل اسی جگہ میں قیمت لگا دیں جہاں شکار قتل ہونے کا واقعہ ہوا ہے۔ کیونکہ جگہوں کے اختلاف کی وجہ سے قیمتیں مختلف ہو جاتی ہیں۔ پس اگر قتل ہونے کی جگہ جنگل ہو جہاں شکار فروخت نہیں ہوتا تو اس سے قریب کی جگہ جہاں شکار بیچا اور خریدا جاتا ہے اعتبار کیا جائے گا۔ مشائخ نے کہا کہ ایک عادل کافی ہے۔ اور دو ہونا بہتر ہے۔ کیونکہ اس میں زیادہ احتیاط اور غلطی سے دوری ہے اور کہا گیا کہ یہاں نص سے دو عادل ہونا معتبر ہے۔
Translation: And the two just men should make the valuation in the place where he (the hunter) struck the game, because prices vary with different locations. If the location is a desert where game is not sold, then the nearest place where game is bought and sold is considered. The scholars said that one just man suffices, but two is better because it is more cautious and farther from error, as in the rights of servants. And it is said that here two are required by the text.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage lays down the procedural rule for the valuation of the killed game in the penalty for hunting. The two just men (or one) must estimate the market value of the game at the location where it was killed, not at a different place. This is because the value can differ based on locality. If the killing occurred in a desert where game is not traded, then they should consider the nearest town or market where such game is sold. The passage also notes a difference of opinion: is one just man sufficient, or must there be two? The majority of scholars (mashā'ikh) say one is sufficient, but two is more precautionary and reduces the chance of error, by analogy with the rights of people (hugūq al-'ibād) where one witness is acceptable in some cases. Others say that the Quranic text (fi'l-āyah) requires two ('ذوا عدل') so two are necessary. This reflects a difference in interpretation of the requirement in the verse (al-Ma'idah 5:95) which uses the dual 'ذوا عدل' (two just men). It is more precautionary to have two, but the operative view (muftā bihi) is that one is sufficient for the valuation, though two are preferred.

Key Terms
تقويم (taqwīm): Estimation of market value of the killed game for the purpose of determining the penalty.
عدل (ʿadl): A just (upright) person whose testimony is acceptable; here used for the person(s) estimating the value.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a hunter kills game in a desert where no game is sold, where should the two just men estimate the value?
A) At the nearest city where game is traded
B) At the location of the killing only
C) At the Kaaba
D) Anywhere convenient

Key Takeaway
One just man suffices for valuation of killed game in Hajj, but two is recommended; the valuation must be at the place of killing or the nearest market if the place is remote.

Place of Slaughtering the Hady
Ruling that hady must be slaughtered within the Haram of Makkah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that hady must be slaughtered in Makkah, cite the Quranic proof, and explain why feeding as an alternative can be done anywhere using the distinction between qurbah ghayr maʿqūlah and maʿqūlah.

Core Idea
Hady is a fixed ritual (ghayr maʿqūlah), so it is restricted to Makkah; feeding is rational (maʿqūlah), so it is universal.

This lesson focuses on a key rule of Hajj penalties: where must the hady (offering animal) be slaughtered? The Hanafi school holds that it must be within the Haram of Makkah, based on the Quranic command 'reaching the Kaaba.' However, the alternative of feeding the poor can be done anywhere. We will explore the proof, the reasoning behind the restriction, and why Imam al-Shafi'i differed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its object
Read the passage: 'وَالْهَدَى لَا يُذْبَحُ إِلَّا بِمَكَّةَ' – the hady must not be slaughtered except in Makkah. This is a binding condition for the validity of the hady.
The ruling applies to all types of hady: penalty for hunting, tamattu', etc.
2
Locate the scriptural proof
The proof is the Quranic verse 'هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ' (an offering reaching the Kaaba). The phrase 'bāligha al-kaʿbah' indicates the hady must physically reach the Kaaba area, i.e., be slaughtered within the Haram.
This is a qatʿī al-dalālah proof – clear and unambiguous regarding location.
3
Contrast with the feeding option
The passage states 'وَيَجُوزُ الإِطْعَامُ فِى غَيْرِهَا' – giving food (iṭʿām) is permissible outside Makkah. This specifies that when the penalty is fulfilled through feeding, location is not restricted.
The Hanafi school treats iṭʿām as a rationally understood act (maʿqūlah), hence general.
4
Understand the Shafi'i disagreement and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes iṭʿām to hady, requiring both in the Haram. The Hanafi refutation: hady is 'qurbah ghayr maʿqūlah' (a prescribed ritual whose wisdom is not fully grasped), so it is tied to a specific place/time; charity is 'maʿqūlah' (benefit understood), so it is valid wherever need exists.
This distinction is central to Hanafi usul regarding taʿabbudī vs. taʿaqqulī acts.
5
Apply the ruling to a real scenario
If a pilgrim violates ihram by hunting, they must offer a hady. They must ensure the animal is slaughtered in Makkah (e.g., by sending money to a butcher there). However, if they choose to feed the poor as expiation, they can do so in their home country.
The consequence of slaughtering outside Makkah: the obligation remains unfulfilled.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہدی کو کہاں ذبح کیا جائے
وَالْهَدَى لَا يُذْبَحُ إِلَّا بِمَكَّةَ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى هَدْياً بَالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ وَ يَجُوزُ الإِطْعَامُ فِى غَيْرِهَا خِلَافًا لِلشَّافِعِي هُوَ يَعْتَبِرُهُ بِالْهَدْيِ وَالْجَامِعُ التَّوَسُعَةُ عَلَى سُكَّانِ الْحَرَمِ وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ الْهَدَى قُرْبَةٌ غَيْرُ مَعْقُوْلَةٍ فَيَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَانٍ أَوْزَمَانٍ أَمَّا الصَّدَقَةُ قُرْبَةٌ مَعْقُولَةٌ فِي كُلِّ زَمَانٍ وَمَكَانِ
ترجمہ اور ہدی ذبح نہ کی جائے مگر مکہ میں ۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے هـديـاً بـالـغ الكعبة اور طعام دینا مکہ کے علاوہ میں بھی جائز ہے ۔ خلافا للشافعی کہ وہ اسے ہدی کے ساتھ قیاس کرتا ہے ۔ اور جامع یہ ہے کہ اس کا تعلق مکہ والوں پر وسعت ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ ہدی ایک قربت ہے جو معقول نہیں ہے پس وہ ایک خاص وقت یا مکان کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے ۔ رہا صدقہ وہ ایک قربت ہے جو معقول ہے ۔ پس وہ ہر وقت اور ہر جگہ ہے
Translation: And hady should not be slaughtered except in Makkah, due to His saying: 'an offering reaching the Kaaba'. And giving food is permissible elsewhere, contrary to al-Shafi'i, who analogizes it to hady. The common reason (jāmiʿ) is the expansion upon the inhabitants of the Haram. We say: hady is an act of worship that is not rationally understood (ghayr maʿqūlah), so it is specific to a place or time. As for charity, it is a rationally understood act of worship, so it is valid in every time and place.
Source pages p. 458

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on the location for slaughtering the hady (the animal offered as penalty for hunting or as part of Hajj). The Hanafi position is that hady must be slaughtered within the boundaries of the Haram of Makkah, specifically in Makkah itself. The proof is the Quranic verse 'هدياً بالغ الكعبة' (an offering reaching the Kaaba), which indicates that the hady must reach the Kaaba area. Conversely, the alternative of feeding the poor (iṭʿām) can be done anywhere, even outside Makkah. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed, holding that the feeding must also be in the Haram, by analogy (qiyas) with the hady. The Hanafi response distinguishes between hady and charity (ṣadaqah). Hady is an act of devotion (qurbah) that is 'ghayr maʿqūlah'—its rationale is not fully understood by human reason; it is a prescribed ritual. Therefore, it is restricted to a specific place and time as appointed by the Lawgiver. Charity, on the other hand, is 'maʿqūlah'—its benefit (helping the poor) is rationally understood, so it is valid wherever the need exists. Thus, feeding the poor as part of the penalty can be done anywhere, while the slaughter of the hady is confined to Makkah.

Key Terms
هدي (hady): An animal offered as a sacrifice in the Haram, either as a penalty (jazā') or for tamattu'/qirān.
قربة غير معقولة (qurbat ghayr maʿqūlah): An act of worship whose underlying rationale is not fully comprehensible by human intellect; it is performed as a pure act of obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where must the hady (offering animal) be slaughtered?
A) In any place where the hunter killed the game
B) In Makkah only
C) In the nearest city to the place of killing
D) In the hunter's hometown

Key Takeaway
Hady is a prescribed ritual tied to the Haram; its slaughter is restricted to Makkah, while the alternative of feeding is flexible due to its rational basis.

Location of Feeding in Hunting Compensation: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on location of it'am vs. hady

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between rational (ma'qul) and irrational (ghayr ma'qul) acts of worship and apply the Hanafi rule that only ghayr ma'qul acts are restricted to a specific location.

Core Idea
Rational worship (it'am) is location-free; irrational worship (hady) is Haram-bound.

This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute on the location of feeding (it'am) as compensation for hunting while in ihram. The Hanafi school, following Al-Quduri, holds that feeding the poor can be done anywhere, while Imam al-Shafi'i restricts it to the poor of Mecca. The key to the dispute lies in the classification of acts of worship: rational (ma'qul) versus irrational (ghayr ma'qul). Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school, as per Al-Quduri, permits feeding the poor anywhere, not restricted to the Haram.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i restricts feeding to the poor of Mecca by analogizing it to hady, which must be slaughtered in the Haram based on the Qur'anic verse 'hadyan baligha al-Ka'bah'.
The common illa (cause) is to provide ease to the residents of the Haram.
3
Follow the opponent's dalil
Understand the qiyas: hady is restricted, so it'am should be restricted because both aim to benefit the Haram residents.
4
Analyse the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafis argue that hady is ghayr ma'qul (irrational worship) and thus tied to place; it'am is ma'qul (rational) and not tied. Therefore, the qiyas is invalid because one cannot analogize a rational act to an irrational one.
This is a methodological point about the limited scope of qiyas.
5
Determine thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Muhrim can feed the poor outside Mecca according to Hanafis, but must feed only the poor of Mecca according to Shafi'is.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جائز ہے۔ امام شافعی کا اختلاف ہے۔ وہ طعام کو ہدی پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ اور جامع حرم کے رہنے والوں کو وسعت دینا ہے اور ہم کہتے ہیں که بدی عبادت غیر معقولہ ہے لہذاوہ کسی مکان یا زمان کے ساتھ مختص رہے گی۔ رہا صدقہ تو وہ عبادت معقولہ ہے ہر زمان اور مکان میں ۔ تشریح قدوری کہتے ہیں کہ جزاء صید میں اگر ہدی کو اختیار کیا گیا تو ہدی کا جانور فقط حرم کے اندر ذبح کیا جا سکتا ہے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کا قول ہے هَدْياً بالِغَ الْكَعْبَةِ ، آیت میں عین کعبہ مراد نہیں بلکہ حرم مراد ہے۔ اور اگر کھانا دینایا کھلانا اختیار کیا تو وہ حرم اور غیر حرم دونوں جگہ جائز ہے حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اطعام بھی فقراء مکہ کے علاوہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی اطعام کو ہدی پر قیاس کرتے ہیں کہ جس طرح ہدی کا ذبح کرنا حرم کے علاوہ میں جائز نہیں ہے اسی طرح غیر حرم کے فقراء کو کھانا کھلانا بھی جائز نہیں ہے۔ اور ہدی اور اطعام کے درمیان علت مشتر که باشندگان حرم پر توسع پیدا کرنا ہے۔ ہماری طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ ہدی غیر معقول قربت و عبادت ہے۔ لہذا کسی زمان یا مکان کے ساتھ خاص رہے گی اور صدقہ ہر زمان اور ہر جگہ عبادت معقولہ ہے۔ پس ایک معقول چیز کو غیر معقول پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہو سکتا ہے۔
It is permissible. Imam al-Shafi'i disagreed. He analogizes feeding to hady. And the purpose is to provide ease to the residents of the Haram. We say that hady is an irrational worship, so it remains restricted to a place or time. As for charity, it is a rational worship, valid in every time and place. Explanation: Al-Quduri said that in compensation for hunting, if hady is chosen, the animal can only be slaughtered inside the Haram because Allah says: 'a hady reaching the Ka'bah' – the verse means the Haram, not the Ka'bah itself. If feeding or giving food is chosen, it is permissible in both Haram and non-Haram. Imam al-Shafi'i says that feeding is also not permissible except to the poor of Mecca. He analogizes feeding to hady: just as hady cannot be slaughtered outside the Haram, similarly feeding poor outside the Haram is not permissible. The common cause between hady and feeding is to provide ease to the residents of the Haram. Our response is that hady is an irrational act of worship, so it remains specific to a time or place, whereas charity is a rational worship in every time and place. So how can a rational thing be analogized to an irrational one?
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the compensation (jaza') for hunting while in ihram. The issue is whether feeding the poor (it'am) as compensation is restricted to the poor of the Haram (Mecca) like the sacrifice (hady) is restricted to the Haram, or if it can be done anywhere. The Hanafi position, as stated by Al-Quduri, is that if one chooses hady, the animal must be slaughtered in the Haram, as per the Qur'anic verse 'hadyan baligha al-Ka'bah' (meaning the Haram). However, if one chooses to feed the poor (it'am), it is valid anywhere, because charity is a rational worship ('ibadah ma'qulah) that is not tied to a specific location. Imam al-Shafi'i analogizes feeding to hady, arguing that both aim to provide benefit to the residents of the Haram, so both should be restricted to the Haram. The Hanafi rebuttal is that hady is an irrational worship (ghayr ma'qulah), meaning its meaning and purpose are not fully comprehensible by human intellect, and thus it is tied to specific conditions like place and time. In contrast, charity (sadaqah) is a rational worship whose purpose (feeding the poor) is understood, so it is not restricted to any place. Therefore, measuring an action that is ma'qul (rational) against one that is ghayr ma'qul (irrational) is invalid. This establishes the Hanafi view that it'am is permissible anywhere.

Key Terms
جَزَاء الصَّيْد (jaza' al-sayd): Compensation for hunting while in ihram, which can be by sacrificing an animal (hady), feeding the poor (it'am), or fasting (sawm).
هَدْي (hady): An animal sacrificed as a religious offering, specifically in the context of Hajj or compensation for hunting.
إِطْعَام (it'am): Feeding the poor as compensation for hunting; giving food to the needy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi response to Imam al-Shafi'i in the passage, why is feeding (it'am) not restricted to the Haram like hady?
A) Because the Qur'an does not mention feeding.
B) Because feeding is a rational worship while hady is irrational.
C) Because the poor outside the Haram are also deserving.
D) Because the Prophet (peace be upon him) allowed it.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the classification of an act as rational (ma'qul) or irrational (ghayr ma'qul) determines whether it is restricted by location; thus, feeding (it'am) is not Haram-bound, unlike sacrifice (hady).

Fasting for Hunting Compensation is Valid Anywhere
Brief ruling with a concise rationale

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on where fasting for jaza' al-sayd may be observed and explain the rationale based on the nature of worship.

Core Idea
Fasting for hunting compensation is valid anywhere because it is an act of worship that can be performed in any location.

The text establishes a clear ruling: if a Muhrim chooses fasting as compensation for hunting, location is irrelevant. Unlike the sacrifice of a hady animal, which must be slaughtered within the Haram, fasting is a devotional act that retains its validity everywhere. This distinction rests on the principle that certain acts of worship are place-agnostic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and its Ruling
Pinpoint the act (fasting for jaza' al-sayd) and the ruling: it is permissible (ja'iz) outside Mecca.
The ruling is stated positively: 'يَجُوزُ' indicates permission.
2
Understand the Rationale
Analyze the reason given: 'because it is worship in every place' (قربة في كل مكان). This contrasts with acts that require a specific location (e.g., hady).
The rationale links the ruling to the intrinsic nature of fasting as a form of worship not tied to place.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَالصَّومُ يَجُوزُ فِى غَيْرِ مَكَةِ لِأُتَهُ قُرَبَةٌ فِي كُلِّ مَكَانٍ
And fasting is permissible in other than Mecca because it is an act of worship in every place.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This is a straightforward ruling statement from the text. It establishes that if a person chooses fasting as the compensation for hunting, there is no restriction on where the fast can be observed. Unlike hady, which must be slaughtered in the Haram, fasting is like feeding (it'am) in that it is a rational form of worship. Therefore, the Muhrim can fast anywhere, whether in Mecca, Medina, or elsewhere. The phrase 'قربتہ فی کل مکان' (it is worship in every place) underscores that the validity of fasting is not contingent upon a specific location. This ruling is part of the Hanafi position in contrast to any view that might restrict all compensations to the Haram.

Key Terms
صَوْم (sawm): Fasting as one of the three options for jaza' al-sayd.
قُرْبَة (qurbah): An act of worship that draws one closer to Allah.

Slaughtering hady outside Haram counts as it'am
Ruling on slaughtering compensation animal outside Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that slaughtering a hady animal outside the Haram does not fulfill the hady obligation but may count as it'am if the meat is given in charity with equivalent value.

Core Idea
Slaughtering outside Haram fails as hady but may count as it'am if meat value equals food required.

This passage addresses a specific scenario: a pilgrim who owes a hady as compensation for hunting cannot simply slaughter the animal anywhere. The Hanafi ruling clarifies that slaughter outside the Haram does not substitute for hady, but the meat, if given in charity, can serve as the it'am option. The key distinction lies in the spilling of blood (iraqah) versus the distribution of meat.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is slaughtering a hady animal outside the Haram (e.g., in Kufa). The ruling: it does not fulfill hady but is considered as it'am if the meat is given as charity with sufficient value.
2
Understand the condition
The condition for it to count as it'am: the meat must be given as charity (sadaqah) and its value must equal the required food value for it'am (which is feeding 60 poor people or similar).
3
Identify the legal reason
The text states 'because the spilling of blood (outside the Haram) does not substitute.' This indicates that the act of slaughter (iraqah) without the animal reaching the Haram is insufficient for hady.
This reasoning is based on the principle that hady requires the animal to reach the Haram.
4
Apply the principle
Hady requires the animal to be slaughtered in the Haram. Outside, the slaughter is not acceptable for hady, but the meat can fulfill the it'am option if given in charity, provided the value matches.
5
Note the practical consequence
The three options (hady, it'am, sawm) are not interchangeable arbitrarily. Each has specific conditions. This ruling shows that one cannot simply slaughter anywhere and expect it to count as hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ ذَبَحَ بِالْكُوفَةِ أَجْرَاهُ عَنِ الطَّعَامِ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ بِاللَّحْمِ وَفِيْهِ وَفَاء بِقِيمَةِ الطَّعَامِ لأنَّ الإرَاقَةَ لَا تُنوب عنه
If he slaughters in Kufa, it is considered as food (it'am). Its meaning: when he gives the meat as charity, and in it there is fulfillment of the value of the food, because the spilling of blood (outside the Haram) does not substitute for it.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling regarding a scenario where a person who owes hady as compensation for hunting slaughters the animal outside the Haram (e.g., in Kufa). The Hanafi ruling is that this act does not fulfill the obligation of hady because hady requires slaughter within the Haram. However, if the meat is distributed as charity (sadaqah) to the poor, and the value of the meat equals the amount of food that would have been given as it'am (the second option), then it is considered as if he has performed the it'am option. The reason is that the spilling of blood (dhabh) itself cannot substitute for hady outside the Haram; hady requires the animal to reach the Haram. But the meat, when given as charity, can fulfill the food requirement if it meets the value. This shows that the three options (hady, it'am, sawm) are not interchangeable in all respects; each has its own rules.

Key Terms
إِرَاقَة (iraqah): Spilling of blood; here refers to slaughtering the animal outside the Haram, which is not sufficient for hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It fulfills the hady obligation because the animal was slaughtered.
B) It is invalid because the animal must be alive.
C) It does not count as hady, but if he gives the meat in charity equal to the value of the food, it counts as it'am.
D) He must repeat the slaughter in the Haram.

Key Takeaway
Slaughtering a hady animal outside the Haram does not fulfill the hady obligation, but the meat can serve as it'am if given in charity with equivalent value.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Young Animals for Hady
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hady animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether young animals (sigar al-ni'am) are acceptable for hady and explain the basis of disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
For hady, only animals valid for udhiyah suffice; young animals are not hady but can be given as charity according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

When a Muhrim must offer hady as compensation, what type of animal is acceptable? The Hanafi school has an internal difference: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf restrict hady to animals that meet the age requirements for udhiyah, while Imam Muhammad allows young animals based on Sahabah practice. This lesson unpacks the ruling and the reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the default requirement: the animal for hady must be one that is valid for udhiyah (e.g., camel 5 years+, cow 2 years+, goat 1 year+, sheep 1 year+).
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Note that Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf maintain the general rule, while Muhammad al-Shaybani allows young animals (sigar al-ni'am) as hady, citing Sahabah practice.
Al-Shafi'i agrees with Muhammad.
3
Examine the evidence for each side
Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf argue that the absolute name 'hady' refers to udhiyah-valid animals. Muhammad argues that the Sahabah assessed young goats and sheep as compensation, implying their validity.
The Sahabah practice is interpreted differently by each side.
4
Understand the it'am alternative
According to the majority, young animals are not acceptable as hady but can be slaughtered and given as charity (it'am) to fulfill the compensation obligation.
This is a secondary option, not the primary hady.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: only udhiyah-valid animals suffice for hady; young animals are only for it'am.
This is the default fatwa in the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا وَقَعَ الْإِحْتِيَارُ عَلَى الْهَدْيِ يَهْدِى مَا يُجْزِيهِ فِى الْأَضْحِيَةِ لِأَنَّ مُطْلَقَ إِسْمِ الهَدَى مُنْصَرِفٌ إِلَيْهِ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدُ وَالشَّافِعِيُّ يُجْزِى صِغَارَ النِّعَمِ فِيهَا لِأَنَّ الصَّحَابَةَ أَوْ جَبُوا عُنَا فَا وَجَفْرَةً وَعِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأبى يُوسُفَ يَجُوز لصَّغَارُ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَطْعَامِ يَعْنِي إِذَا تَصَدَّقَ
And when the choice falls on hady, he should give what is sufficient in udhiyah (sacrifice), because the absolute name of hady refers to it. Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said: Young cattle are sufficient in it, because the Companions made obligatory a 'unafah' (young goat) and a 'jafrah' (young sheep). And according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, young [animals] are permissible on the basis of food (it'am), meaning when he gives in charity.
Source pages p. 459

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute (as well as an inter-madhhab one with al-Shafi'i) regarding what type of animal is acceptable for hady when chosen as compensation for hunting. The base ruling: the animal should be one that is valid for udhiyah (sacrifice) - e.g., a camel five years old, a cow two years old, a goat one year old. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that young animals (like a young goat or a four-month-old sheep) are also acceptable for hady, citing that the Companions (Sahabah) had assessed young animals as compensation. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that young animals are only permissible 'ala wajh al-it'am' (on the basis of feeding), meaning if the animal is slaughtered and the meat is given as charity in the amount equivalent to the food value. In other words, young animals cannot fulfill the hady obligation directly; they can only be used to fulfill the it'am option. The difference stems from interpreting the Sahabah's action: Muhammad and al-Shafi'i see it as allowing any animal for hady; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf view it as a case where the young animal was used for feeding, not hady per se. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that for hady, only animals valid for udhiyah are acceptable; young animals are not sufficient unless they are treated as food.

Key Terms
أُضْحِيَة (udhiyah): The animal sacrificed on Eid al-Adha; the standard for animals acceptable for hady.
صِغَار النِّعَم (sigar al-ni'am): Young cattle (e.g., kids, lambs) that are less than the typical age for udhiyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, how are young animals (sigar al-ni'am) acceptable for compensation?
A) As hady, directly fulfilling the hady obligation.
B) As it'am, by giving the meat in charity.
C) They are not acceptable at all.
D) Only for fasting.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi Hanafi position is that only animals valid for udhiyah are acceptable for hady; young animals (sigar al-ni'am) can only be used for feeding (it'am).

Minimum Food Amounts in Hunting Compensation (It'am)
Ruling on the amount of food to give to each poor person

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum amount of food to give per poor person in it'am for hunting compensation and explain the rationale based on Shariah custom.

Core Idea
Each poor person must receive at least half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley.

This lesson clarifies the specific quantities required when a hunter chooses to feed the poor as compensation for killing game. The amounts are not arbitrary but derived from Shariah customs, ensuring consistency with other obligations like zakat al-fitr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is it'am (feeding) as an option for jaza' al-sayd. The ruling is that specific minimum amounts apply per poor person.
2
Note the types of food and amounts
The text specifies: half a sa' of wheat, or one sa' of dates, or one sa' of barley.
These are the only permissible types mentioned.
3
Understand the rationale
The amounts are based on what is customary in Shariah (al-ma'huud fi al-shar'), referring to the same measures used in sadaqat al-fitr and kaffarat.
4
Recognize the prohibition
It is not permissible (la yajuz) to give any poor person less than the specified minimum, as that would not fulfill the obligation.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage explains the details of the it'am (feeding) option for jaza' al-sayd. First, the value of the hunted animal (the one killed) is assessed, and that value is used to purchase food. It is not permissible to give less than this to any individual poor person. The basis for these specific amounts is that the word 'ta'am' (food) in the Qur'anic verse is understood by reference to what is customary in Shariah, which is the same as in sadaqat al-fitr and kaffarat al-yamin. This ensures consistency across similar obligations. The food must be given to multiple poor people until the total value is exhausted; the text does not specify a number, but the principle is to give each poor the specified amount until the value is fully distributed.

Key Terms
صَاع (sa'): A measure of volume, equivalent to approximately 3.6 liters or 2.5 kg for wheat in Hanafi fiqh.
نِصْف صَاع (nisf sa'): Half a sa' of wheat, approximately 1.8 liters or about 1.25 kg.

Number of Fasts for Hunting Compensation
Ruling on fasting quantity for hunting compensation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of compensatory fasts required for hunting in ihram, given the value of the hunted animal measured in food units.

Core Idea
One fast per half sa' of wheat or per sa' of dates/barley.

This passage gives the rule for fasting as an option for jaza' al-sayd (compensation for hunting while in ihram). After estimating the hunted animal's value in terms of food (wheat, dates, or barley), one must fast for each half sa' of wheat or each full sa' of dates/barley. This lesson clarifies the method and the counting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the compensation option
Note that the pilgrim has three options from Quran 5:95: slaughter an equivalent animal, feed poor, or fast. The passage assumes fasting is chosen.
The fasting option is only valid if the pilgrim is able to fast.
2
Estimate the animal's value as food
Two just persons evaluate the hunted animal and determine its monetary value, then convert to food units: either half sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley.
The food equivalent is based on the staple food of the region.
3
Count the food units
Each half sa' of wheat equals one unit. For dates or barley, each full sa' equals one unit. So if the value equals 3 half-sa' of wheat, that's 3 units; if 2 sa' of dates, that's 2 units.
Wheat units are half sa', while dates and barley are full sa'.
4
Apply the fasting rule
Fast for one day per unit. Therefore, the number of fasts equals the number of units. If the value is 4 half-sa' of wheat, fast 4 days.
The fasts are obligatory once chosen; they need not be consecutive but should be completed.
5
Verify with example
Example: An animal worth 5 half-sa' of wheat requires 5 fasts. An animal worth 3 sa' of dates requires 3 fasts.
Always convert first to the correct unit (half sa' for wheat, full sa' for dates/barley).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he chooses fasting, he estimates the killed [animal] as food, then he fasts for every half sa' of wheat or sa' of dates or barley [?].
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage presents the third option for jaza' al-sayd: fasting (sawm). The method is as follows: first, the value of the hunted animal is estimated in terms of food (i.e., how many half sa' of wheat or whole sa' of dates/barley does its value equal). Then, for each half sa' of wheat (or equivalent in dates/barley), the person must fast one day. For example, if the animal's value equals five half-sa' of wheat, then five fasts are required. This is consistent with the principle that each day of fasting substitutes for feeding one poor person the specified amount. The OCR cuts off, but the Urdu commentary confirms the pattern: fasting for each half sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley. This ruling aligns with the Qur'anic verse (5:95) which gives the option of fasting, and the Hanafi school specifies the number of days based on the food equivalent.

Key Terms
صِيَام (siyam): Fasting as compensation for hunting; each day of fasting substitutes for feeding one poor person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 5 fasts
B) 10 fasts
C) 2.5 fasts
D) Depends on the animal type

Key Takeaway
The number of compensatory fasts for hunting is determined by the food-equivalent value: one fast per half sa' of wheat or per sa' of dates/barley.

The Age Requirement for Hadi: Adult vs. Young Animals
Dispute on age of animals valid for Hadi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the Hanafi position (Shaykhayn) from the views of Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i regarding the permissibility of young animals for Hadi, and state the relied-upon ruling with its practical consequence.

Core Idea
Hadi follows Udhiyah: only adult animals qualify; young animals are permissible only as food for the poor.

This lesson tackles a nuanced intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute about the age of animals that can be offered as Hadi – the sacrificial penalty for a muhrim who hunts during Hajj. While the Quran uses the absolute term 'Hadi', the school's authoritative position (Shaykhayn) insists that only adult animals meeting Udhiyah conditions suffice. However, Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i argue otherwise, citing Companion practice. Understanding how the Hanafi school reconciles these proofs reveals a key principle in Fiqh: the distinction between the sacrificial act and the alternative of feeding the poor.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position (Shaykhayn)
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf: Hadi must be an adult animal meeting the conditions for Udhiyah (camel 5+, cow 2+, goat 1+). Young animals are not valid as Hadi itself.
The absolute word 'Hadi' is understood by custom to refer to adult sacrificial animals.
2
Identify the Opposing View and Its Basis
Imam Muhammad (within Hanafi) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that young animals (e.g., a goat kid, a four-month lamb) are valid for Hadi. Their evidence: the Companions made such animals wajib as Hadi.
They rely on practice (dalil naqli) not explicit Quran/Hadith text.
3
Analyze the Hanafi Response to the Opposing Dalil
The Shaykhayn reinterpret the Companion examples: those were not cases of Hadi as a sacrifice, but cases where animals were slaughtered and given as food to the poor (the second option in the hunting penalty).
This reconciliation preserves the absolute nature of 'Hadi' while honoring the Companion reports.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf (Practical Consequence)
The difference matters in practice: a muhrim who chooses to offer Hadi must give an adult animal. If he chooses to feed the poor (equivalent value), he may slaughter a young animal and distribute the meat.
This clarifies the mufta bihi position and avoids confusion.

Source Text

Small animals on the basis of feeding, meaning when he gives charity. Translation: And when the killer's choice falls on giving Hadi, he gives what is permissible for Udhiyah. The absolute word Hadi refers to that. Imam Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said that small young of livestock are also permissible in this Hadi, because the Companions made a small goat kid and a four-month-old lamb wajib. And according to the two Shaykhs, small animals are permissible on the basis of giving food, i.e., when he gives charity. Explanation: The issue is that if the hunter of game chooses to give Hadi, then the animal that suffices for Udhiyah is sufficient, e.g., a five-year-old camel, a two-year-old cow, and a one-year-old goat. Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i said that slaughtering younger animals for Hadi is also permissible, because the Companions made 'anaq (a goat kid) and jafrah (a four-month-old lamb) wajib for Hadi. Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the age of animals valid for Hadi (the sacrificial animal given as penalty for hunting). The base ruling: if the muhrim chooses to offer Hadi, it must be an animal that meets the conditions for Udhiyah (sacrificial animal on Eid), which are adult animals: camel 5 years, cow 2 years, goat 1 year. This is because the word 'Hadi' in the Quran is absolute and it is understood to mean the animal well-known in the Shariah for sacrifice. Imam Muhammad and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that young animals (kids and lambs) are also valid for Hadi, citing the practice of the Companions. The two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that young animals are not valid as Hadi itself, but they can be slaughtered and their meat distributed as food (on behalf of the poor). Thus, the dispute is settled: if one chooses Hadi, adult animals are required; if one chooses to feed the poor (the second option), then young animals are permissible because the requirement is merely to give food equivalent to the value.

Key Terms

عناق ('anāq): A young goat kid, before one year.
جفرہ (jafrah): A lamb that is four months old.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Hadi for the hunting penalty requires an adult animal meeting Udhiyah conditions; young animals are permissible only as charity (food for the poor).

Amount of Food Given to Each Poor Person in Hunting Penalty
Ruling on food distribution amounts and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum amount of food per poor person (half sa' wheat or one sa' dates/barley) in the hunting penalty and identify the Shariah basis for these measures.

Core Idea
The minimum food per poor person in hunting penalty is fixed: half sa' wheat or one sa' dates/barley, based on the customary Shariah practice.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on how much food must be given to each poor person when a muhrim chooses feeding as compensation for unlawful hunting. The passage specifies precise measures rooted in the Shariah tradition, derived from the interpretation of 'food' in the Quran and consistent with other expiations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
The ruling is on the amount of food per poor person when feeding is chosen as the penalty. The passage states that each poor receives half sa' wheat or one sa' dates/barley, and giving less is not permissible.
This is a wajib amount.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is the Quranic verse (5:95) mentioning 'food' (ta'am). The Hanafi school interprets this 'food' to refer to the customary amounts known from other Shariah obligations like sadaqat al-fitr and kaffarah.
The proof is textual but requires interpretation (urf shar'i).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The word 'food' is ambiguous; the Hanafi school argues that it must be understood in light of Shariah customs (urf). The established custom defines the minimum per person as these specific measures.
This is an application of the principle that ambiguous terms are clarified by prevailing practice.
4
Note the Ikhtilaf
There is a difference of opinion: other schools may allow different amounts or other food items. The Hanafi position is relied upon.
The passage uses 'indana' (according to us), signaling a potential divergence.
5
Evaluate the Tarjih
The Hanafi position is considered the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) due to its consistency with other Shariah expiations and the preservation of the spirit of the penalty.
The tarjih is implicit in the text; later scholars confirm this.

Source Text

Calculating Fasts in Hunting Penalty
Ruling on number of fasts when fasting option chosen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of fasts required for the hunting penalty using the food-based method and explain the rationale for the remainder rule.

Core Idea
Fasts for hunting penalty are calculated via food equivalents: one day per half sa' wheat, with remainder options.

When a muhrim chooses the fasting option for hunting a game animal, the number of days is not directly assessed. Instead, the Shariah uses a two-step method: first estimate the game's value in food, then convert that food into fasting days. This method mirrors the fidya rules for Ramadan and ensures practical feasibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the penalty option chosen
The muhrim has three options: sacrifice, feed the poor, or fast. This passage addresses when fasting is selected.
2
Estimate the game's food value
Determine the market value of the killed game, then convert that value into food (wheat, dates, or barley) using the same rates as the feeding option.
The food estimation is already explained in previous sections.
3
Convert food to fasts
For every half sa' of wheat (or one sa' of dates/barley) equivalent, one day of fasting is required. This conversion is based on the parallel to fidya.
4
Handle remainder less than half sa'
If after conversion there is a remainder of food less than half a sa', the muhrim has a choice: give that amount in charity or fast an entire extra day. Partial day fasting is not legislated.
5
Apply the rule for total obligation less than one poor person's food
If the entire food obligation is less than the minimum for one poor person (i.e., less than half sa'), the muhrim may either feed that small amount or fast one full day.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إنِ اخْتَارَ القِيامَ يَقُومُ الْمَقْتُولَ طَعَامًا ثُمَّ يَصُومُ عَنْ كُلّ نِصْفِ صَاعٍ مِنْ بُرٍ أَوْ صَاعٍ مِنْ تَمَرٍ أَوْ شَعِي...  ... تَقْدِيرِ المِ بِالْمَقْتُولِ غَيْرُ مُمْكِن إِذْ لَا قِيْمَةَ لِلصَّيَامِ فَقَدَّرُ نَاهُ بِالطَّعَامِ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ عَلى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ مَعْهُودُ فِى الشَّريعَ كَمَا فِى بَابِ الْفِدْيَةِ فَإِنْ فَضْلَ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ أَقَلَّ مِنْ نِصْفِ صَاعِ فَهُوَ مُخَيَّرُ إِنْ شَاءَ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَامَ عَنْهُ يَوْمًا كَامِلا لأنَّ الصَّوْمَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعِ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ كَانَ الْوَاجِبُ دُونَ طَعَامِ مِسْكِينٍ يُطْعِمُ قَدْرَ الْوَاجِبِ أوْ يَصُومَ يَوْمًا كَامِلًا لِمَا قُلْنَا
If he chooses fasting, he estimates the killed [game] in terms of food, then he fasts for every half sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley... Estimating the [fast] by the killed is not possible since there is no value for fasting, so he estimated it by food. And estimation in this manner is customary in Shariah, as in the chapter of fidya. If there remains less than half sa' of food, he has the choice: if he wishes, he may give it in charity, and if he wishes, he may fast a full day for it, because fasting less than a day is not legislated. Similarly, if the obligation is less than one poor person's food, he feeds the amount of the obligation or fasts a full day for what we have said.
Source pages p. 460

Commentary
This passage explains the third option: fasting. Since fasting has no market value, it is impossible to directly equate the game with days of fasting. Therefore, the Shariah uses an indirect method: first estimate the value of the game in terms of food (as done in the feeding option), then for every half sa' of wheat (or one sa' of dates/barley), one day of fasting is required. This method is already established in Shariah for similar situations like fidya (ransom). If after calculating the food amount, there is a remainder less than half a sa', the muhrim has a choice: either give that small amount in charity, or fast a whole extra day. This is because partial day fasting is not prescribed. Similarly, if the total obligation is less than the food for one poor person (i.e., less than half sa'), he may either give that small amount or fast a full day. The rationale is the same: one cannot fast less than a full day.

Key Terms
فدیہ (fidyah): Ransom or compensation, especially for missed fasts due to old age.
صاع (sa'): A unit of volume measure, approximately 2.5–3 kg for wheat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the game's value equals 3 half-sa' of wheat, how many fasts must the muhrim observe?
A) 3 fasts
B) 1.5 fasts
C) 6 fasts
D) 2 fasts

Key Takeaway
Fasts for hunting penalty are calculated by converting the game's food value into days: one day per half sa' wheat or one sa' dates/barley, with a special rule for leftovers less than half sa'.

Partial Damage to Game: Proportional Compensation
Ruling on compensation for partial game damage with qiyas proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on compensation for damaging game without killing, distinguishing between partial reduction and full value when escape ability is lost.

Core Idea
Compensation for game defects is wajib: proportional for partial loss, full value if escape ability is destroyed.

When a muhrim damages game without killing, the Hanafi school imposes compensation based on the extent of harm. This lesson examines two scenarios: minor defects requiring proportional payment and severe defects destroying escape ability requiring full value. The ruling is founded on qiyas from human rights.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the muhrim did (wound, pluck hair, cut limb) and apply the ruling: pay reduction in value. Then identify if the act destroyed escape ability (plucking bird's feathers, cutting legs) — then pay full value.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to compensation in human rights ('as in the rights of human beings'). The principle of 'part is analogous to whole' applies.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The 'illa (effective cause) is the loss of a part or quality that reduces value. When escape ability is lost, the security is destroyed, so full compensation is due.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars may require full value only if the game actually dies. The Hanafi position imposes full value when escape ability is lost, even if still alive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ جَرَحَ صَيدًا أوْنَتَفَ شَعْرَهُ أوْ قَطَعَ عُضْرًا مِنْهُ ضَمِنَ مَا نَقَصَهُ اِعْتِبَارًا للبَعْضِ بِالكُلّ كَمَا فِى حُقوقِ الْعِبَادِوَ لَوْ نَتَفَ رِيْشَ طَائِرٍ أَوْ قَطَعَ قَوَائِمَ صَيْدٍ فَخَرَجَ مِنْ خِيْرِ الْاِمْتِنَاعِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ فَوَّتَ عَلَيْهِ الْأُمِّنَ يَتَفوِيتِ الَةِ الْاِمْتِنَاعِ فَيَغْرَمُ جَزَاءً
And if he wounds a game animal, or plucks its hair, or cuts a limb from it, he is liable for the reduction [in value], by analogy of the part to the whole, as in the rights of human beings. And if he plucks the feathers of a bird, or cuts the legs of a game animal so that it loses its ability to escape, then on him is the full value, because he has caused its security to be lost by destroying the means of escape, so he pays the compensation.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This passage addresses the case where the muhrim does not kill the game but causes a defect. The principle is that he must pay compensation equal to the reduction in the animal's market value due to the defect. This is analogous to how damages are calculated in human rights (e.g., if someone injures another, they pay the difference in value). However, if the defect is so severe that the animal loses its ability to escape (e.g., plucking a bird's flight feathers so it cannot fly, or cutting the legs of a land animal so it cannot run), then the muhrim must pay the full value of the animal. This is because although the animal is still alive, it has been rendered defenseless and will inevitably die or be captured, so the security it had is destroyed. Full compensation is due.

Key Terms
ضمان (ḍamān): Liability to pay compensation for damage or loss.
خيار الامتناع (khiyār al-imtināʿ): The ability to escape; the means of self-preservation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Full value of the rabbit
B) Reduction in value
C) Nothing, because it is still alive
D) Depends on whether the rabbit dies later

Key Takeaway
When a muhrim damages game, compensation is wajib: proportional for minor defects, full value if escape ability is destroyed.

Converting Game Value to Fasting Days in Hunting Compensation
Explains the conversion from game value to food to fasting days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the number of fasting days required for hunting compensation (jaza) and apply the rule for fractional leftovers less than half a sa' of food.

Core Idea
Fasting days are estimated via food value — each half-sa' equals one fast, and any smaller residue triggers a full day's fast or charity.

When a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) kills game and chooses the option of fasting as compensation (jaza), the number of fasting days cannot be determined directly because fasting has no monetary value. Instead, Islamic law uses an intermediary: the game is first valued in terms of food (ta'am), then each half-sa' of that food (or equivalent) is counted as one fasting day. This method is established by analogy (qiyas) to the fidya (expiation) for broken fasts. Once you understand this conversion, you can precisely calculate the required fasting days, including what to do with fractional leftovers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its context
The passage addresses the compensation (jaza) for killing game while in ihram. The ruling is that fasting is one of the three options (along with sacrificing an animal or feeding the poor). The calculation method is based on the value of the game.
The Qur'anic basis is Surah al-Ma'idah 5:95, which mentions equivalence from livestock or feeding the poor or fasting.
2
Understand the qiyas (analogy) to fidya
The Hanafi school uses qiyas to the chapter of fidya (expiation for missed fasts). In fidya, if a person cannot fast, they feed one poor person half a sa' of wheat (or one sa' of dates/barley) per day. Here, the game's value is first converted into food (ta'am), then each half-sa' equals one fasting day.
The asl (original case) is fidya; the far' (new case) is hunting compensation; the illa (effective cause) is the need to estimate compensation via food.
3
Apply the conversion rate
Once the game is valued in terms of food (e.g., price of the game in wheat), calculate how many half-sa' units that food amount contains. Each complete half-sa' requires one fasting day. For example, if the food equivalent is 2 sa', that equals 4 half-sa' units, so 4 fasting days.
The half-sa' is approximately 1.25 kg of wheat; the sa' is about 2.5 kg.
4
Handle fractional leftovers
If after dividing by half-sa', there is a remainder of less than half a sa', the muhrim has a choice: he may give that remaining food in charity, or he may fast one full day for that remainder. The reason is that fasting less than one full day is not prescribed in Islamic law.
The same rule applies if the entire food equivalent is less than half a sa' — he may give it in charity or fast one full day.
5
Note the rationale and final ruling
The passage concludes that this method is consistent with the Sharia's approach to estimation where direct valuation is impossible. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is this calculation method: convert game to food, then to fasting days, with the option for leftovers.
This is based on the Zahir al-Riwayah texts and is the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تَقْدِيرُ الصَّوْمِ بِالْمَقْتُولِ غَيْرُ مُمْكِن إِذْ لَا قِيْمَةَ لِلصَّيَامِ فَقَدَّرْنَاهُ بِالطَّعَامِ وَالتَّقْدِيرُ عَلَى هَذَا الْوَجْهِ مَعْهُودٌ فِى الشَّرِيعَةِ كَمَا فِى بَابِ الْفِدْيَةِ فَإِنْ فَضْلَ مِنَ الطَّعَامِ أَقَلَّ مِنْ نِصْفِ صَاعٍ فَهُوَ مُخَيَّرٌ إِنْ شَاءَ تَصَدَّقَ بِهِ وَإِنْ شَاءَ صَامَ عَنْهُ يَوْمًا كَامِلاً لِأَنَّ الصَّوْمَ أَقَلَّ مِنْ يَوْمٍ غَيْرُ مَشْرُوعٍ وَكَذَلِكَ إِنْ كَانَ الْوَاجِبُ دُونَ طَعَامِ مِسْكِينٍ يُطْعِمُ قَدْرَ الْوَاجِبِ أَوْ يَصُومَ يَوْمًا كَامِلًا لِمَا قُلْنَا
The estimation of fasting by the killed [game] is not possible since there is no value for fasting, so we estimated it by food. And estimation in this manner is customary in the Sharia, as in the chapter of fidya. So if there remains less than half a sa' of food, he has the choice: if he wishes, he may give it in charity, and if he wishes, he may fast a full day for it, because fasting less than a day is not legislated. Similarly, if the obligatory [amount] is less than the food of one needy person, he gives the amount obligatory or fasts a full day for what we have said.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This is a ruling_with_proof passage from the book of Hajj concerning the compensation (jaza) for killing game while in ihram. The author addresses the scenario where the pilgrim chooses the option of fasting instead of sacrificing or giving charity. The key issue is how to determine the number of fasting days. Since fasting has no monetary value, it cannot be directly equated to the game's value. Therefore, the Sharia employs an intermediary: first, the game is valued in terms of food (ta'am). The method is well-established in Islamic law, similar to the fidya (expiation) for breaking a fast. The rate is: one day of fasting for each half sa' of wheat (or one sa' of dates or barley). If after calculating the food equivalent, there is a remainder of less than half a sa', the pilgrim has a choice: either give that small amount in charity or fast a full day for it, because fasting less than a full day is not prescribed. Similarly, if the entire obligatory amount is less than half a sa', the same option applies. The reasoning is that the minimum unit of valid fasting is one full day.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game animal hunted in the state of ihram
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation for killing game while in ihram
صاع (sa'): A measure of volume, approximately 2.5 kg for wheat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fasting days for hunting compensation are determined by converting the game's value into food, with each half sa' requiring one fast, and leftovers less than half sa' give the option of charity or an extra full fast.

Liability for Injuring Game Without Killing
States the ruling on partial damage to game and full value when defense is lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on partial damage to game by stating the compensation for injury and identifying when full value is due.

Core Idea
Injuring game in ihram requires compensation for reduction; if defense lost, full value.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah clarifies that the obligation to compensate (damān) for hunting prohibitions extends beyond killing to injuries. The author uses qiyas (analogy) to civil damages to establish the rule that partial injury requires proportional compensation, while severe injury that prevents the animal from escaping triggers full value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is injuring a game animal (wounding, plucking hair, cutting an organ) while in ihram. The ruling is that the muhrim must compensate the reduction in value caused by the injury.
Note that partial damage is treated by analogy to the whole, not as a separate category.
2
Understand the proof (dalil)
The author uses qiyas (analogy) to the rights of people (huquq al-'ibad): just as partial damage to someone's property requires proportional compensation, so too with game.
This is a qiyas jaliy (clear analogy) because the illa (effective cause) is the loss or reduction of value.
3
Distinguish the special case
If the injury is so severe that the animal loses its ability to defend itself or escape (e.g., plucking a bird's feathers or cutting its limbs), then the muhrim must pay the full value of the game.
The reason (illa) is that by destroying the means of defense, the muhrim has effectively caused the animal's loss of security, which is akin to destroying it entirely.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
For example, if a muhrim cuts the tail of a deer (minor injury), he pays the reduction in value. If he breaks both legs of a rabbit (rendering it immobile), he pays the full value.
Threshold: the animal must be rendered unable to escape; minor injuries that do not affect escape ability only trigger partial compensation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ جَرَحَ صَيْدًا أَوْ نَتَفَ شَعْرَهُ أَوْ قَطَعَ عُضْوًا مِنْهُ ضَمِنَ مَا نَقَصَهُ اعْتِبَارًا لِلْبَعْضِ بِالْكُلِّ كَمَا فِي حُقُوقِ الْعِبَادِ وَلَوْ نَتَفَ رِيشَ طَائِرٍ أَوْ قَطَعَ قَوَائِمَ صَيْدٍ فَخَرَجَ مِنْ خَيْرِ الِامْتِنَاعِ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ لِأَنَّهُ فَوَّتَ عَلَيْهِ الْأَمْنَ بِتَفْوِيتِ آلَةِ الِامْتِنَاعِ فَيَغْرَمُ جَزَاءً
And if he wounds a game, or plucks its hair, or cuts an organ from it, he guarantees what he reduced, considering the part by analogy to the whole, as in the rights of people. And if he plucks the feathers of a bird, or cuts the limbs of a game, so it leaves the state of being able to defend itself, then upon him is its full value, because he caused it to lose its security by destroying the means of defense, so he pays the compensation.
Source pages p. 461

Commentary
This ruling_with_proof passage addresses the scenario where a muhrim injures game without killing it. The general principle is that the muhrim is liable for the reduction in value caused by his action. This is derived by qiyas (analogy) to the rules of damages in civil law (huquq al-'ibad): if someone damages another's property partially, he compensates the loss; similarly, if he damages the game partially, he compensates the reduction. The text then presents a specific case: if the injury is so severe that the animal loses its ability to escape (e.g., by plucking feathers of a bird or cutting its limbs), then the muhrim is liable for the full value of the game. This is because by destroying the means of defense, he effectively caused its death (since the animal will likely die or be captured). Thus, he is treated as if he killed it.

Key Terms
ضمان (damān): Guarantee or liability to compensate for damage
امتناع (imtina'): Ability to defend oneself or escape

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Partial injury requires proportional compensation; total loss of defense requires full value.

Ruling on Breaking an Ostrich Egg and Related Cases
States the ruling on compensation for breaking an ostrich egg and analogous cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for breaking an ostrich egg during ihram and explain how istihsan overrides qiyas when a dead chick emerges.

Core Idea
When an ostrich egg is broken in ihram, by istihsan the value of the chick is due if a dead chick emerges, not just the egg's value.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses the compensation (dam) for a muhrim who breaks an ostrich egg. The ruling is based on a Companion narration and a principle of precaution. The key legal reasoning involves a conflict between qiyas and istihsan, where istihsan prevails due to the egg's preparation for life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and base ruling
The act is breaking an ostrich egg while in ihram. The base ruling is that the muhrim must pay the value of the egg. This is from a narration of Ali and Ibn Abbas and because the egg is the origin of game, treated as game by precaution.
The egg must not be spoiled.
2
Note the dalil (evidence)
The ruling is supported by the practice of the Companions (qawl al-sahabi), which is a valid proof in Hanafi fiqh, though zanni in transmission and meaning.
3
Understand the qiyas position
By qiyas (analogy to general property law), if a dead chick emerges from the broken egg, only the egg's value is due because the chick's life was not certain at the time of breaking.
The illa (effective cause) is uncertainty of life.
4
See the istihsan rationale
Istihsan overrides qiyas because the egg is naturally prepared to produce a living chick, and the breakage causes its death prematurely. Therefore, the chick's death is attributed to the breaker as a precaution, and he owes its full value.
This is a stronger consideration than the uncertainty of life.
5
Extend to the gazelle case
The same principle applies if a muhrim strikes a pregnant gazelle, causing the death of the fetus and the mother. He must pay the full value of the mother (including the fetus) because the strike caused the death.
The value includes both mother and fetus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ كَسَرَ بَيْضَ نَعَامَةٍ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ وَهَذَا مَرْوِيٌّ عَنْ عَلِيٍّ وَابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ وَلِأَنَّهُ أَصْلُ الصَّيْدِ وَلَهُ عُرْضِيَّةٌ أَنْ يَصِيرَ صَيْدًا فَنَزَلَ مَنْزِلَةَ الصَّيْدِ احْتِيَاطًا مَا لَمْ يَفْسُدْ فَإِنْ خَرَجَ مِنَ الْبَيْضِ فَرْخٌ مَيْتٌ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهُ وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ وَالْقِيَاسُ أَنْ لَا يَغْرَمَ سِوَى الْبَيْضَةِ لِأَنَّ حَيَاةَ الْفَرْخِ غَيْرُ مَعْلُومٍ وَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ الْبَيْضَ مُعَدٌّ لِيَخْرُجَ مِنْهُ الْفَرْخُ الْحَيُّ وَالْكَسْرُ قَبْلَ أَوَانِهِ سَبَبٌ لِمَوْتِهِ فَيُحَالُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ احْتِيَاطًا وَعَلَى هَذَا إِذَا ضَرَبَ بَطْنَ ظَبْيَةٍ فَأَلْقَتْ جَنِينًا مَيْتًا وَمَاتَتْ فَعَلَيْهِ قِيمَتُهَا
And whoever breaks an ostrich egg, upon him is its value. And this is narrated from Ali and Ibn Abbas. And because it is the origin of the game, and it has the potential to become game, so it is treated in the status of game as a precaution, as long as it is not spoiled. Then if a dead chick comes out from the egg, upon him is its value. And this is istihsan. And the qiyas is that he does not pay anything except the egg, because the life of the chick is unknown. The basis of istihsan is that the egg is prepared for a living chick to emerge from it, and the breakage before its time is a cause for its death, so it is attributed to him as a precaution. And upon this, if he strikes the belly of a gazelle and it throws a dead fetus and dies, then upon him is its value.
Source pages p. 462

Commentary
This ruling_with_proof passage deals with compensation for breaking an ostrich egg while in ihram. The ruling is based on narrations from Ali and Ibn Abbas, and on the principle that the egg is the source of the game (asl al-sayd) and has the potential to become game. Therefore, as a precaution, it is treated like game as long as it is not spoiled. If a dead chick emerges from the broken egg, the muhrim must pay the value of the chick. This is by istihsan (juristic preference). The qiyas (analogy) would suggest that only the egg's value is due, because the chick's life was not certain. However, istihsan prevails because the egg is naturally prepared to produce a live chick, and the breakage caused its death prematurely. Therefore, the chick's value is attributed to the breaker. The same ruling applies if one strikes the belly of a pregnant gazelle, causing a dead fetus and the mother's death: full value of the mother (including the fetus) is due.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason
قياس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an existing ruling to a new case
بيض (bayd): Egg (of an ostrich in this context)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a muhrim breaks an ostrich egg and a dead chick comes out?
A) He pays only the value of the egg.
B) He pays the value of the chick by qiyas.
C) He pays the value of the chick by istihsan.
D) No compensation is due because the chick was not alive.

Key Takeaway
When an unspoiled ostrich egg is broken in ihram, the muhrim pays the egg's value; if a dead chick emerges, by istihsan he pays the chick's value, and the same applies to striking a pregnant gazelle.
