Animals a Muhrim May Kill Without Penalty
Ruling with proof on animals a muhrim may kill without penalty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five core animals exempt from penalty in ihram, apply the Hanafi criterion of initiating harm to determine inclusion, and explain why the magpie and monitor lizard are not exempt.

Core Idea
A muhrim may kill harmful animals without penalty; the Hanafi school includes all dogs and mice by genus, and only excludes those that do not initiate harm.

In this lesson, we examine a crucial exception to the general prohibition on hunting in ihram. The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly permitted killing certain harmful animals. The Hanafi school expands this permission based on the underlying cause (illah) of harm, and we will see how the scholars distinguish between exempt and non-exempt creatures.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states that killing seven named animals incurs no penalty (jaza'). Understand that this is an exception to the general prohibition on killing game while in ihram.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
Examine the hadith cited: 'Five harmful creatures are killed in halal and haram.' Note that the hadith lists five animals but the text lists seven. The additional animals (wolf, crow) are included based on other narrations and interpretation.
The wolf is either the intended meaning of 'biting dog' or mentioned in other reports.
3
Analyse the inclusion criteria
The key criterion is that the animal 'begins with harm' (yabtadi' bi al-adha). Apply this to the crow: only the impurity-eating crow qualifies, not the magpie. Similarly, the monitor lizard and jerboa do not initiate harm and are thus not exempt.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's position on genus
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that all dogs (biting or non-biting, tame or wild) and all mice (domestic or wild) are the same by genus (jins). Therefore, any dog or mouse is exempt, regardless of specific harmfulness.
This is an intra-Hanafi clarification; the text does not record disagreement from the Sahibayn.
5
Distinguish exempt from non-exempt animals
Compile the list: crow (impurity-eating), kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, dog. Exclude: magpie, monitor lizard, jerboa, and any other animal that does not initiate harm.
The exemption is specific; do not extend it to animals not mentioned or not meeting the criterion.

Source Text

ایذاء دینے میں پہل نہیں کرتے ہیں۔ تشریح شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری نے فرمایا ہے کہ اگر محرم نے کوے یا چیل یا بھیڑئیے یا سانپ یا بچھو یا چو ہے یا کٹ کھنے کتے کو مارڈالا تو اس پر کوئی جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔ دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا یہ فرمان ہے کہ آپ نے پانچ بدکار جانوروں کوحل اور ترم دونوں میں قتل کرنے کی اجازت دی ہے ( چیل، سانپ ، بچھو، چوہا اور کٹ کھنا کتا )۔ دوسری حدیث یہ ہے کہ چوہے ، کوئے چیل ، بچھو، سانپ اور کلب عقور کو محرم قال کر سکتا ہے۔ یہاں یہ اشکال ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے محرم کے لئے جانورں کو قتل کرنے سے منع کیا ہے مگر پانچ کا استثناء کیا ہے یعنی پانچ وقل ی اجازت دی ہے۔ اور دوسری حدیث میں چھ شمار کرائے ہیں اس کا جواب اول فصل میں دیا جا چکا ہے ۔ وَقَد ذكر الذنب الخ سے بھی
ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ بخاری اور مسلم کی احادیث میں ذئب کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ پس مصنف قدوری نے ذئب کا اضافہ اپنی طرف سے کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحیحین کے علاوہ بعض روایات میں ذئب مذکور ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحیحین کی حدیث میں جو کلب عقولہ ہے اس سے مراد ذئب ہے۔ یا یوں کہا جائے کہ ذئب کلب عقور کے معنی میں ہے۔
ساحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں غراب سے مراد وہ کوا ہے جو کبھی نجاست کھاتا ہے اور کبھی دانہ کھاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ نجاست ہی سے آغاز کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ بھی نجاست خوار کے مانند ہوا۔ اور رہاوہ کو ا جو سیاہ اور سفید ہوتا ہے اور اس کی آواز لفظ عقعق کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، حدیث میں وہ مستثنی نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ غراب نہیں کہلاتا۔ پس اس کو قتل کرنے سے جزاء واجب ہوگی ۔ اور یہ عقعق نجاست سے بھی آغاز نہیں کرتا بلکہ دانہ کھاتا ہے اور اسی کو اپنی غذاء میں ترجیح دیتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ عدم وجوب جزاء میں کلب عقور اور غیر عقور اور پالتو اور وحشی سب برابر ہیں۔ کیونکہ معتبر جنس کلب اور حقیقت کلب سب میں موجود ہے۔ اسی طرح گھر یلو چوہا اور وحشی سب غراب ہیں ۔ اور گوہ اور جنگلی چوہا ان پانچ میں نہیں ہیں جن کا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں جانور ایذاء دینے میں ابتداء نہیں کرتے ہیں۔
And there is no penalty in killing the crow, the kite, the wolf, the snake, the scorpion, the mouse, and the biting dog, because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Five harmful creatures are killed in the state of halal and haram: the kite, the snake, the scorpion, the mouse, and the biting dog.' And he said, peace be upon him: 'The muhrim kills the mouse, the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the snake, and the biting dog.' And the wolf has been mentioned in some narrations. And it is said that what is meant by 'biting dog' is the wolf, and it is said that the wolf is in its meaning. And what is meant by 'crow' is that which eats carrion and mixes, because it begins with harm. As for the magpie, it is not exempted, because it is not called a crow and does not begin with harm. And from Abu Hanifa: that the biting dog and the non-biting, the tame and the wild, are the same, because the consideration in that is the genus. Similarly, the domestic mouse and the wild one are the same. And the monitor lizard and the jerboa are not among the five exempted, because they do not begin with harm. Translation: And there is no penalty for killing crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, and biting dog, because the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Five harmful animals are killed in halal and haram: kite, snake, scorpion, mouse, and biting dog.' And the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'The muhrim kills the mouse, the crow, the kite, the scorpion, the snake, and the biting dog.' And in some narrations the wolf is mentioned. And it is said that by 'biting dog' is meant the wolf, or it is said that the wolf is in the meaning of biting dog. And by 'crow' is meant that which eats impurity and mixes grain, because it takes the initiative in harm. As for the magpie, it is not excepted, because it is not called a crow and does not take the initiative in harm. And it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that the biting dog and the non-biting, the domesticated and the wild, are all equal, because the genus is considered. Similarly, domestic mouse and wild mouse are equal. And the monitor lizard and the jerboa are not among the five that are excepted, because these two do not take the initiative in causing harm. Explanation: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri said: If a muhrim kills a crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, or biting dog, no penalty is due. The proof is the Prophet's statement that he permitted killing five harmful animals in halal and haram: kite, snake, scorpion, mouse, and biting dog. Another hadith is that the muhrim can kill the mouse, crow, kite, scorpion, snake, and biting dog. Here there is an objection: The Prophet prohibited killing animals for the muhrim but excepted five; so he allowed five. In the second hadith six are counted. The answer to this has been given in the first chapter. And 'wa qad dhukira al-dhi'b' etc. is also an answer to a question. The question is: In the narrations of Bukhari and Muslim, the wolf is not mentioned. So the author al-Quduri added the wolf from himself. The answer is that besides the two Sahihs, the wolf is mentioned in some narrations. The second answer is that in the hadith of the two Sahihs, the 'biting dog' refers to the wolf, or it is said that the wolf is in the meaning of biting dog. The author of al-Hidayah says: In the hadith, by 'crow' is meant the crow that sometimes eats impurity and sometimes eats grain, because it starts with impurity. So it is like an impurity-eater. As for the magpie, which is black and white and its sound is with the word 'aq'aq', it is not included in the exception because it is not called a crow. Therefore, killing it incurs a penalty. And this magpie does not begin with impurity but eats grain and prefers it as its food. A narration from Imam Abu Hanifa is that in the non-obligation of penalty, the biting dog and non-biting, domesticated and wild, are all equal, because the genus dog and the reality of dog is present in all. Similarly, domestic mouse and wild mouse are all [the same]. And the monitor lizard and the jerboa are not among the five that the Prophet excepted, because these two animals do not take the initiative in causing harm.
Source pages p. 463

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, stating that a muhrim (person in ihram) may kill certain harmful animals without incurring any penalty (jaza'). The ruling is based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) listing five (or six) harmful creatures that may be killed in both the halal and haram states. The text then clarifies the types of crow and dog included. The crow must be the type that eats carrion and begins with harm; the magpie (aq'aq) is not included. For the dog, Abu Hanifa holds that all types—biting, non-biting, tame, wild—are the same because the genus is considered. Similarly, all mice are the same. The monitor lizard (dabb) and jerboa (yarbu') are not among the exempted five because they do not begin with harm. The commentary by al-Quduri and al-Marghinani (sahib al-Hidayah) explains the proofs and resolves the apparent discrepancy between the hadiths mentioning five and six animals.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): Penalty or compensation due for violating ihram prohibitions, such as killing game.
فواسق (fawasiq): Harmful or sinful creatures that are allowed to be killed even in ihram.
كلب عقور (kalb 'aqur / 'afur): A dog that bites or is predatory; according to some, specifically the wolf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Crow that eats carrion

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may kill only those harmful animals specifically exempted by the Prophet or those that share their genus and meet the criterion of initiating harm; all others require penalty.

Insects a Muhrim Can Kill Without Penalty
Ruling with rational proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing harmful and non-harmful insects while in ihram and explain why no penalty is due.

Core Idea
A muhrim can kill harmful insects without penalty because they are neither game nor body-born.

During Hajj or Umrah, a pilgrim in ihram must avoid hunting game (sayd) and killing certain creatures. But what about mosquitoes, ants, and fleas? This lesson clarifies that these insects do not incur any penalty when killed, based on a clear rational distinction from game and body-born parasites.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine which insects are covered and whether killing them is permissible. The text lists mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks.
For harmful ants (black and yellow), killing is permissible; for non-harmful ants, it is not permissible but still no penalty.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is a rational argument: penalty would be due only if the insect were game (sayd) or generated from the body. Since these insects are neither, no penalty applies.
The text uses a two-factor test: sayd and mutawallid min al-badan.
3
Trace the reasoning
Understand why game and body-born creatures incur penalty. Game hunting violates the prohibition of sayd; body-born creatures (like lice) are killed to clean the body, which also incurs penalty. These insects lack both reasons.
The harmful nature (mu'dhi) only justifies killing but does not trigger a penalty.
4
Note the distinction for ants
Only harmful ants (black and yellow) may be killed; non-harmful ants should not be killed, but if killed, no penalty is due because they still lack the two characteristics.
The ruling balances permissibility and penalty separately.

Source Text

وَلَيْسَ فِى قَتْلِ الْبَعُوضِ وَالنَّمْلِ وَالْبَراغِيثِ وَالْقَرَادِ شَيْ لأَنَّهَا لَيْسَتْ بِصُيُودٍ وَ لَيْسَتْ بِمُتَوَلِدَةٍ مِنَ الْبَدَنِ ثُمَّ هِيَ مُوْدِيَةٌ بِطَبَاعِهَا وَالْمُرَادُ بِالنَّمْلِ السَّوْدَاءُ وَالصَّفْرَاءُ الَّتِي تُؤْذِى وَمَا لَا يُؤْذِى لَا يَحِلُّ قَتْلُهَا وَلَكِنْ لَا يَجِبُ الْجَزَاء لِلعِلة الأولى ترجمہ اور مچھر ، چیونٹی ، پسو اور چڑی کو قتل کرنے میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ جانور نہ تو صید ہیں اور نہ بدن سے متولد ہیں۔ ہاں یہ اپنی طبیعت سے موذی ہیں۔ اور چیونٹی سے مراد سیاہ چیونٹی یا زرد چیونٹی ہے جو ایذاء دیتی ہے اور جو چیونٹی ایذا نہیں دیتی اس کا قتل کرنا حلال نہیں ہے لیکن جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی علت اولی کی وجہ سے ۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے مچھر یا چیونٹی یا پسو یا چڑی کو مار ڈالا تو اس پر ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ جانور نہ تو صید ہیں اس لئے کہ صید وہ ہوتا ہے جو آدمی سے متوحش ہو۔ اور یہ جانور آدمی سے متوحش نہیں ہوتے بلکہ آدمی کی طرف راغب ہوتے ہیں۔ اور نہ یہ جانور آدمی کے بدن سے پیدا ہوتے ہیں۔ زیادہ سے زیادہ یہ ہے کہ یہ طبعا موذی ہوتے ہیں۔ اگر یہ جانور وحشی ہوتے تو صید کو قتل کرنے کی وجہ سے جزاء واجب ہوتی اور اگر آدمی کے بدن سے پیدا ہوتے تو بدں کی پراگندگی اور میل کچیل کو صاف کرنے کی وجہ سے جزاء واجب ہو جاتی ۔ مگر جب دونوں باتیں نہیں ہیں تو جزاء بھی واجب نہ ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ چیونٹی سے سیاہ چیونٹی یا زرد چیونٹی مراد ہے جو انسان کو ایذاء دیتی ہے۔ اس کو قتل کرنا تو جائز ہے مگر قتل کی وجہ سے جزاء واجب نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور وہ چیونٹی جو کسی کو ایذا نہیں دیتی اس کا قتل کرنا ہی حلال نہیں ہے لیکن اگر قتل کر دیا تو جزاء واجب نہ ہو گی۔ کیونکہ نہ تو یہ صید کے حکم میں ہے اور نہ آدمی کے بدن سے پیدا ہوتی ہے۔
And there is nothing in killing mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks, because they are not game and they are not generated from the body; moreover, they are harmful by their nature. And by 'ants' is meant the black and yellow ones that cause harm; and that which does not cause harm, its killing is not permissible, but no penalty is due because of the first reason. Translation: And there is nothing obligatory in killing mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks, because these animals are neither game nor generated from the body. Yes, they are harmful by nature. And by 'ant' is meant the black ant or yellow ant that causes harm; and the ant that does not cause harm, its killing is not permissible, but no penalty is due because of the first reason. Explanation: If a muhrim kills a mosquito, an ant, a flea, or a tick, no compensation (daman) is due. Because these animals are not game, since game is that which is wild and avoids humans, and these animals are not wild but are attracted to humans. Nor are they generated from the human body. At most, they are naturally harmful. If they were wild, penalty would be due for killing game; if they were generated from the body, penalty would be due because they clean the body's dirt and filth. But since neither applies, no penalty is due. The author of al-Hidayah says: By 'ant' is meant the black ant or yellow ant that harms humans. Killing it is permissible, but no penalty is due. And the ant that does not harm anyone, its killing is not permissible, but if killed, no penalty is due, because it is neither considered game nor generated from the human body.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a ruling stating that a muhrim may kill certain insects (mosquitoes, ants, fleas, ticks) without incurring any penalty. The reasoning is based on two factors: these insects are not considered 'game' (sayd) because they are not wild and avoid humans; they are not generated from the human body (like lice). The only reason they might be killed is because they are naturally harmful (mudhi). The text clarifies that only harmful ants (black and yellow) are permissible to kill; non-harmful ants should not be killed, but if killed, no penalty is due because they still lack the two characteristics. The commentary explains that if these insects were wild, killing them would be like killing game and would require a penalty. If they were body-born, killing them would also incur a penalty because they help clean the body. Since neither applies, there is no penalty.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Game: animals that are wild and avoid humans, and hunting them is normally permissible except in ihram.
متولد من البدن (mutawallid min al-badan): Generated from the body: such as lice, which are born from human filth.
موذی (mu'dhi): Harmful by nature; these insects cause harm and may be killed for that reason.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because it is generated from the body
B) Because it is not considered game and not generated from the body
C) Because it is always permissible to kill insects
D) Because it is not harmful

Key Takeaway
Killing harmful insects in ihram incurs no penalty because they lack the two defining characteristics (game and body-born) that would require compensation.

The Five Excepted Animals in Ihram: Wolf, Crow, and Dogs
Answers question on wolf inclusion, defines crow, states Abu Hanifa's dog ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school includes the wolf among the five excepted animals in ihram and state the ruling on killing dogs based on Imam Abu Hanifa's narration.

Core Idea
Wolf is included via 'kalb aqur'; all dogs are equal in ruling because the genus matters.

This passage clarifies the scope of the five harmful animals that a Muhrim may kill without compensation. It addresses a key question: why did al-Quduri add the wolf when the two Sahihs do not mention it? The answer lies in other narrations and in interpreting 'kalb aqur' as wolf. It also defines which crow is excepted and presents Imam Abu Hanifa's ruling that all dogs are equal.

Guided Path
1
Identify the approved acts and rulings
Determine which animals a Muhrim can kill without incurring compensation. The passage discusses the wolf, crow, dog, magpie, and others.
The five excepted animals are: crow, kite, scorpion, rat, and dog (including wolf).
2
Locate the proofs for inclusion
Examine the hadith evidence. The Sahihayn do not mention the wolf, but other authentic narrations do. The term 'kalb aqur' is interpreted to include the wolf.
This is an example of combining multiple narrations and using linguistic interpretation.
3
Trace the definition of ghurab
Understand why the magpie (aq'aq) is not excepted. The ghurab is only the crow that starts with filth; the magpie does not, so killing it requires compensation.
The defining characteristic is behavior, not just name.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi position on dogs
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that all dogs—biting or not, domestic or wild—are equal in that no compensation is due when killed, because the genus (jins) of dog is the underlying cause.
This is a Nawadir narration; the more widely accepted view may differentiate.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf
Compare the Hanafi ruling on wolf and dogs with the Shafi'i position. The practical difference is whether compensation is required.
This affects a Muhrim's actions in real situations.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب انج ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ بخاری اور مسلم کی احادیث میں ذئب کا ذکر نہیں ہے۔ پس مصنف قدوری نے ذئب کا اضافہ اپنی طرف سے کیا ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحیحین کے علاوہ بعض روایات میں ذئب مذکور ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ صحیحین کی حدیث میں جو کلب عقولہ ہے اس سے مراد ذئب ہے۔ یا یوں کہا جائے کہ ذئب کلب عقور کے معنی میں ہے۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں غراب سے مراد وہ کوا ہے جو کبھی نجاست کھاتا ہے اور کبھی دانہ کھاتا ہے کیونکہ وہ نجاست ہی سے آغاز کرتا ہے۔ اس لئے وہ بھی نجاست خوار کے مانند ہوا۔ اور رہاوہ کو ا جو سیاہ اور سفید ہوتا ہے اور اس کی آواز لفظ عقعق کے ساتھ ہوتی ہے، حدیث میں وہ مستثنی نہیں ہے کیونکہ وہ غراب نہیں کہلاتا۔ پس اس کو قتل کرنے سے جزاء واجب ہوگی ۔ اور یہ عقعق نجاست سے بھی آغاز نہیں کرتا بلکہ دانہ کھاتا ہے اور اسی کو اپنی غذاء میں ترجیح دیتا ہے۔ حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ سے ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ عدم وجوب جزاء میں کلب عقور اور غیر عقور اور پالتو اور وحشی سب برابر ہیں۔ کیونکہ معتبر جنس کلب اور حقیقت کلب سب میں موجود ہے۔ اسی طرح گھر یلو چوہا اور وحشی سب غراب ہیں ۔ اور گوہ اور جنگلی چوہا ان پانچ میں نہیں ہیں جن کا حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے استثناء فرمایا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں جانور ایذاء دینے میں ابتداء نہیں کرتے ہیں۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary on Hidayah, volume three, Kitab al-Hajj. This is an answer to a question. The question is that in the hadith of Bukhari and Muslim, the wolf (dhi'b) is not mentioned. So the author al-Quduri added the wolf on his own. The answer is that besides the Sahihayn, in some narrations the wolf is mentioned. A second answer is that in the hadith of the Sahihayn, what is said 'kalb aqur' (biting dog) is intended to mean wolf. Or it can be said that wolf is in the meaning of biting dog. The author of al-Hidayah says that in the hadith, 'ghurab' refers to the crow that sometimes eats filth and sometimes eats grain, because it begins with filth. Thus it is like a filth-eater. As for the magpie, which is black and white and its sound is with the word 'aq'aq', it is not excepted in the hadith because it is not called a ghurab. So killing it will necessitate compensation (jaza). And this magpie does not begin with filth but eats grain and prefers it as its food. From Imam Abu Hanifa there is a narration that in the non-obligation of compensation, a biting dog and non-biting, domestic and wild, are all equal. Because the genus of dog and the reality of dog is present in all. Similarly, domestic rat and wild one are all ghurab. And the monitor lizard (goh) and field mouse are not among the five which the Prophet (peace be upon him) excepted, because these two animals do not initiate harm.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a clarification of the scope of the five harmful animals that Muhrim is permitted to kill without incurring compensation (jaza). The passage begins by addressing a potential objection: why did al-Quduri include the wolf (dhi'b) in the list when the two Sahihs (Bukhari and Muslim) do not mention it? The answer is that other authentic narrations include the wolf, and also that the term 'kalb aqur' (biting dog) in the Sahihayn is interpreted as wolf, since wolf is a type of biting dog. Then the text defines 'ghurab' (crow) as the black crow that starts with filth, so it is like a filth-eater and is excepted. In contrast, the magpie (aq'aq) is not called ghurab and does not eat filth, so killing it requires compensation. Next, a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa states that all dogs—whether biting or not, domestic or wild—are equal in that no compensation is due when killed, because the underlying cause ('illa) is the genus of dog. Finally, the passage clarifies that the monitor lizard and field mouse are not among the five excepted animals because they do not initiate harm. This is an intra-Hanafi position narrated from Imam Abu Hanifa, and it is relied upon in the school.

Key Terms
ذئب (dhi'b): Wolf, included among the five harmful animals excepted from prohibition in ihram.
غراب (ghurab): Crow that eats both filth and grain, starting with filth. It is excepted in ihram.
کلب عقور (kalb 'aqur): Biting dog or any dog that harms; includes wolf in Hanafi school.
عقعق (aq'aq): Magpie, a black and white bird that does not eat filth. It is not among the excepted animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is not among the excepted animals, so compensation is required.
C) It is permissible only if it attacks, and compensation is required otherwise.
D) It is completely permissible without any compensation because it is a bird.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school extends the five excepted animals to include the wolf via interpretation and additional narrations, and all dogs are considered equal in the ruling of no compensation based on the genus.

Ruling on Killing Harmful Insects in Ihram: No Compensation Required
States the ruling that killing certain insects in ihram incurs no compensation and explains the legal cause.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks in ihram and identify the two conditions that would trigger compensation (sayd or mutawallid).

Core Idea
In ihram, compensation is only due for killing game (sayd) or body-generated creatures; harmful insects fall under neither.

This passage from al-Hidayah addresses a practical question for pilgrims: what happens if you accidentally kill a mosquito or ant while in ihram? The ruling may surprise you—no compensation is required. The text explains the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind this exemption, based on the definition of game (sayd) and creatures generated from the body (mutawallid). Understanding this distinction helps clarify the principles governing compensation in ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and ruling
The passage discusses killing specific insects (mosquitoes, ants, fleas, ticks) while in ihram. The ruling: no compensation (jaza') is due.
2
Understand the two conditions for compensation
According to the Hanafi school, compensation in ihram is required only for two types: game (sayd) and body-generated creatures (mutawallid min al-badan). The passage explains that these insects are neither.
If the animal were sayd or mutawallid, compensation would be obligatory.
3
Analyse the definition of 'sayd'
Sayd refers to wild animals that must be hunted and are shy of humans. These insects are not wild; they are attracted to humans, so they are not sayd.
The passage states that these insects are 'attracted to humans' (راغب ہوتے ہیں).
4
Analyse 'mutawallid min al-badan'
This refers to lice and similar parasites that originate from the body's filth. The listed insects are not generated from the body, so no compensation.
If they were mutawallid, compensating for cleaning the body would be due.
5
Distinguish between harmful and non-harmful ants
The text specifies that harmful ants (black or yellow that bite) may be killed, but non-harmful ants should not be killed; however, even if killed, no compensation is due because the same conditions are absent.
The prohibition on killing non-harmful ants does not change the compensation ruling.

And there is nothing (obligatory) in killing mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks because they are not game (sayd) and they are not generated from the body. Then they are harmful by their nature. And by ants is meant the black and yellow that harm; as for what does not harm, its killing is not lawful, but no compensation is required due to the first cause. Translation: And there is nothing obligatory in killing mosquitoes, ants, fleas, and ticks. Because these animals are neither game nor generated from the body. Yes, they are harmful by nature. And by ants is meant the black or yellow ant that gives harm; and the ant that does not harm, its killing is not lawful but compensation will not be required due to the first cause. Commentary: If a Muhrim kills a mosquito, ant, flea, or tick, then no guarantee (daman) is obligatory upon him. Because these animals are not game, since game is that which is wild from humans, and these animals are not wild but are attracted to humans. Nor are they generated from the human body. At most, they are naturally harmful. If these animals were wild, then compensation would be due for killing game; and if they were generated from the body, then compensation would be due for cleaning the body's filth. But since both are absent, compensation is not obligatory. The author of al-Hidayah says: by ants is meant the black ant or yellow ant that harms humans. Killing it is permissible, but no compensation is required due to killing it. And the ant that does not harm anyone, its killing is not lawful (halal), but if one kills it, no compensation is required, because it is neither in the ruling of game nor is it generated from the human body.
Source pages p. 464

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with its proof regarding the killing of small insects (mosquitoes, ants, fleas, ticks) while in ihram. The main ruling: no compensation (jaza or daman) is due. The text provides two reasons: (1) they are not game (sayd), because game is defined as an animal that must be captured by hunting and is wild towards humans, whereas these insects are not wild—they actually seek humans; (2) they are not generated from the human body (like lice). If they were either of these, compensation would be due. However, they are naturally harmful (mu'dhiya bi taba'iha), which makes their killing permissible but not subject to compensation. The text clarifies that ants are of two types: harmful (black or yellow) and non-harmful. Killing harmful ants is permissible and no compensation; killing non-harmful ants is not halal (haram) but still no compensation is required, because the condition for compensation is missing. The commentary expands on the definition of game and the absence of the two causes.

Key Terms
صید (sayd): Game: an animal that is wild and must be captured by hunting; it is not tame towards humans.
متولد (mutawallid): Generated from the body; refers to parasites like lice that originate from human bodily filth.
جزاء (jaza'): Compensation required for killing certain animals while in ihram; can be a sacrificial animal or charity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is no compensation (jaza) required for killing a mosquito in ihram according to the Hanafi school?
A) Because mosquitoes are not game and not generated from the body.
B) Because mosquitoes are too small to matter.
C) Because mosquitoes are not mentioned in the Quran.
D) Because all insects are automatically excepted.

Key Takeaway
In ihram, compensation is only required for game (sayd) and body-generated creatures; harmful insects are exempt.

Killing Lice in Ihram: Charity at Will
Ruling with proof on killing lice in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a louse in ihram and explain the proof from al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
Killing a louse in ihram requires charity, but the amount is discretionary—a handful suffices.

Lice are unique among insects because they are generated from the body's filth. While in ihram, killing a louse triggers a light obligation of charity, not a fixed penalty. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from the core Hanafi text al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
What act is being ruled? Killing a louse (qamlah) while in ihram. The ruling is wajib charity (sadaqah) at the discretion of the Muhrim.
2
Locate the proof
The author cites al-Jami' al-Saghir from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: 'At'im shay'an' (Feed something). This is a command from the Prophet (peace be upon him) transmitted through Imam Muhammad.
The proof is a hadith ahad, making the ruling zanni al-thubut, hence wajib not fard.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
In Hanafi usul, the imperative (amr) indicates obligation (wujub). The word 'shay'an' (something) is general, so any food item suffices—no minimum measure is specified.
This differs from other acts where a specific amount is required.
4
Understand the illa (reason)
Lice are 'mutawallid min al-nataf'—generated from the filth on the body. Killing them is akin to cleaning the body, which obligates charity by analogy (qiyas).
The illa is the filth origin, not the act of killing per se.
5
Note the practical limit
The author gives a minimal example: a handful (kaff) of food. Some later scholars specified one handful for up to three lice and half a sa' for more, but the mufta bihi is any amount one wishes.
The charity does not need to be filling (mushbi').

And whoever kills a louse should give charity as he wishes, like a handful of food, because it is generated from the filth that is on the body. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Feed something.' For example, he should give a handful of grain. And some scholars have said that for two or three lice, give one handful of wheat, and for more than that, give half a sa' of wheat. Therefore, in the case of killing a louse or throwing it to the ground, it is obligatory to give some grain as charity. Al-Jami' al-Saghir says: 'Feed something' — give something. This statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that feeding a poor person by way of permission is sufficient; filling his stomach is not a condition.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the expiation (jaza) for killing lice while in ihram. The main ruling: one must give charity (sadaqah) at will, and the minimal example given is a handful of food. The reason (illa) is that lice are generated from the filth on the body, so killing them is akin to cleaning the body, which obligates charity. The text references al-Jami' al-Saghir (a core book of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad) to support that one must feed something, but it does not require a full meal; any small amount is acceptable by way of permission (ibaha). The commentary adds that if one kills a louse by hand from the head or body, or even throws it to the ground and kills it, the same ruling applies. Some scholars differentiate quantities: for up to three lice, one handful of wheat; for more, half a sa'. The underlying principle is that lice are mutawallid (generated from the body), unlike the previous insects which were not. So compensation is due, but it is light — left to the discretion of the Muhrim.

Ruling on Killing a Locust in Ihram: Giving Charity at Will
States ruling with proof from Umar's qawl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a locust in ihram and apply the proof from Umar's statement to determine sufficient charity.

Core Idea
Killing a locust in ihram requires charity — even a single date fulfills the obligation.

When a Muhrim kills a locust, a common question arises: is compensation required, and if so, how much? This passage from al-Hidayah clarifies that the locust is considered land game (sayd al-barr), so its killing triggers an obligation to give charity. However, the amount is left to the individual's discretion, with a historical precedent from Umar ibn al-Khattab that even a single date suffices. This lesson unpacks the ruling, the proof, and the practical application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is killing a locust (jaradah) while in a state of ihram. The ruling applies specifically to a Muhrim, not to a non-Muhrim.
2
Determine the ruling (hukm)
The hukm is wajib: the Muhrim must give charity (sadaqah). The amount is discretionary (ma sha'a), meaning he may choose what to give, but a minimum is indicated.
Charity is wajib, not fard, because the proof is zanni (single sahabi statement).
3
Locate the proof (dalil)
The proof is the statement of Umar ibn al-Khattab: 'A date is better than a locust.' This shows that even a date is sufficient, implying charity is required.
The proof is a qawl sahabi, considered zanni in thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the legal cause (illa)
The locust is classified as land game (sayd al-barr) because it can only be caught by a trick (hilah) and the catcher intends to catch it. As game, its killing in ihram requires compensation.
This definition distinguishes locust from insects like mosquitoes, which are not game.
5
Apply the minimal amount
Based on Umar's statement, giving a single date (tamrah) for one locust is sufficient. The historical context: people of Hims were giving a dirham, but Umar considered that excessive.
The amount is not fixed; any charitable item of similar value suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَتَلَ جَرَادَةً تَصَدَّقَ بِمَا شَاءَ لِأَنَّ الْجَرَادَ مِنْ صَيْدِ الْبَرِّ فَإِنَّ الصَّيْدَ مَا لَا يُمْكِنُ أَخْذُهُ إِلَّا بِحِيلَةٍ وَيَقْصِدُهُ الْآخِذُ وَتَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ لِقَوْلِ عُمَرَ تَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ
ترجمہ اور جس محرم نے ٹڈی مار ڈالی وہ جو چاہے صدقہ کرے اس لئے ٹڈی خشکی کا شکار ہے کیونکہ شکار وہ کہلاتا ہے جس کا پکڑنا بغیر حیلہ کے ممکن نہ ہو اور پکڑنے والا اس کا ارادہ کرے اور ایک کھجور ایک ٹڈی سے بہتر ہے کیونکہ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا ہے تَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے ٹڈی مار ڈالی تو جو چاہے صدقہ کرے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ٹڈی خشکی کا شکار ہے۔ کیونکہ شکار وہ کہلاتا ہے جس کا پکڑنا بغیر حیلہ کے ممکن نہ ہو۔ اور پکڑنے والا اس کا ارادہ بھی کرے۔ صاحب قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ ایک کھجور بہتر ہے ایک ٹڈی سے۔ یہ اصل میں حضرت عمر کا قول ہے۔ واقعہ یہ ہے کہ اہل حمص احرام کی حالت میں بکثرت ٹڈی مارتے تھے اور ہر ٹڈی کے عوض ایک درہم صدقہ کرتے تھے ۔ حضرت عمر نے فرمایا اے اہل حمص تمہارے دراہم کثیر ہیں تَمْرَةٌ خَيْرٌ مِنْ جَرَادَةٍ یعنی ایک ٹڈی کے عوض ایک درہم صدقہ کرنا بہت گراں ہے تم لوگ تو اگر ایک ٹڈی کے عوض ایک کھجور صدقہ کر دو، یہ بھی بہت کافی ہے۔
And whoever kills a locust should give charity as he wishes, because the locust is from land game; for game is that which cannot be taken except by a trick and the taker intends it. And a date is better than a locust, due to the statement of Umar: 'A date is better than a locust.' Translation: And whoever Muhrim kills a locust should give charity as he wishes, because the locust is land game. For game is called that which cannot be caught without a trick, and the catcher intends it. And one date is better than one locust, because Umar said: 'A date is better than a locust.' Commentary: If a Muhrim kills a locust, he should give charity as he wishes. The proof is that the locust is land game. Because game is called that which cannot be caught without a trick, and the catcher intends it. Author al-Quduri says: one date is better than one locust. This is originally the statement of Umar. The incident is that the people of Hims used to kill many locusts while in ihram and would give one dirham in charity for each locust. Umar said: O people of Hims, your dirhams are abundant, 'a date is better than a locust' — meaning giving one dirham for one locust is too heavy; if you give one date for one locust, that is very sufficient.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling on killing a locust (jaradah) while in ihram. The ruling: one must give charity (sadaqah) at will, i.e., whatever amount one chooses. The reasoning (illa) is that the locust is considered land game (sayd al-barr) because it requires a trick to catch and the catcher intends to catch it. Since it is game, compensation is due. However, the compensation is minimal. The text quotes the Companion Umar ibn al-Khattab's statement: 'A date is better than a locust,' meaning that even a single date suffices as charity for one locust. The commentary provides the historical context: the people of Hims were giving a dirham per locust, and Umar told them that was excessive; a date is enough. This demonstrates that the compensation for a locust is light and left to the Muhrim's discretion, with the minimum being something like a date. The passage is from the perspective of the Hanafi school, which treats locust as land game even though it is an insect, because it fits the definition of sayd (cannot be caught easily, and is hunted intentionally).

Key Terms
جرادة (jaradah): Locust; considered land game in Hanafi fiqh due to being hunted.
صید البر (sayd al-barr): Land game; animals that live on land and are hunted.
تمرة (tamrah): A date fruit; used as a minimal measure of charity for killing a locust.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) One date (tamrah).
C) A handful of grain.

Key Takeaway
For killing a locust in ihram, charity is obligatory; a date or similar small item is sufficient, as established by Umar's statement.

Expiation for Killing a Louse in Ihram
Ruling on expiation for killing a louse while in ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the expiation for killing a louse in ihram and explain the evidence from al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
Killing a louse in ihram requires giving any small charitable amount; no fixed measure is needed.

Many pilgrims wonder about the minor infractions that occur during ihram, such as killing a louse. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position: a simple charity of any small amount suffices. The proof comes from a direct command in al-Jami' al-Saghir, but the indefinite wording leaves the quantity flexible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is killing a louse (or throwing it to the ground) while in the state of ihram. The ruling is that it incurs a wajib sadaqah.
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary evidence is the statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad: 'Feed something.' This is a command (amr) which in Hanafi usul indicates obligation.
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah
The word 'something' (shay'an) is indefinite, signifying that any small amount is acceptable – there is no fixed measure. The command is for a charitable act, not a specific penalty.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Some Hanafi scholars differentiate amounts: one handful for up to three lice, half a sa' for more. However, the primary view is that any small amount suffices.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The relied-upon position is that giving any small amount to a poor person, like a handful of food, is sufficient. This flexibility is based on the indefinite wording of the hadith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And whoever kills a louse should give charity as much as he wishes, like a handful of food, because it is generated from the dirt that is on the body. And in al-Jami' al-Saghir: 'Feed something.' And this indicates that it suffices him to feed a poor person a small thing by way of permission, even if it is not filling. Explanation: If a muhrim catches and kills a louse from his head or another part of his body, or throws it to the ground, he should give charity as he wishes. For example, he may give a handful of grain. Some scholars have said that for two or three lice he gives a handful of wheat, and for more than that he gives half a sa' of wheat. The proof is that the louse is generated from the dirt that is on a person's body, and charity is obligatory for cleaning dirt. Therefore, killing a louse or throwing it to the ground also makes it obligatory to give some grain as charity. In al-Jami' al-Saghir it says: 'Feed something,' meaning give something. This statement from al-Jami' al-Saghir indicates that feeding the poor person something by way of permission is sufficient; feeding him to fullness is not a condition.
Source pages p. 465

Commentary
This is a ruling on the penalty for killing a louse while in the state of ihram. The author first states the ruling: one should give charity as he wishes, like a handful of food. He then provides the reasoning: lice are generated from the dirt on the body, and removing dirt requires charity (analogy with removing dirt from the body, which requires sadaqah). He cites al-Jami' al-Saghir which says 'feed something,' indicating that the amount is not specified; any small amount suffices even if it does not fill the poor person. The Urdu commentary explains further: if a muhrim kills a louse from his head or body, or throws it to the ground, he must give charity as he wishes, e.g., a handful of grain. Some scholars differentiate quantities: for two or three lice, one handful of wheat; for more, half a sa' of wheat. The underlying illa is that lice originate from dirt, and cleaning dirt (like removing hair or nails) incurs sadaqah. The text emphasizes that the feeding is by way of ibahah (permission), not mandatory fullness, so a small amount suffices.

Key Terms
فَمَّلَةٌ (qummalah): A louse that infests the body or clothes; in this context, a louse killed by a muhrim.
إِبَاحَةٌ (ibāhah): Permissibility; here it means that feeding the poor is not obligatory to the point of fullness, but merely giving something as a charitable act.

No Penalty for Killing a Turtle in Ihram
Ruling on killing a turtle in ihram: no penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on killing a turtle in ihram and explain the two reasons why no penalty is incurred.

Core Idea
A turtle is not game; it can be caught without trickery and is not hunted intentionally, so no penalty in ihram.

This lesson examines a specific ruling for a muhrim who kills a turtle. The Hanafi school clarifies that not every animal killed in ihram requires expiation. By analogy with insects and the definition of game, the turtle is excluded. We will unpack the two lines of reasoning from the classical text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
Locate the specific act: a muhrim slaughtering a turtle. The ruling is that there is no penalty (daman) upon him.
This is the central claim.
2
First rationale: analogy to insects
Turtles are categorized as harmful insects (hawamm) and crawling creatures (hasharat). Killing such creatures in ihram is permissible without fidyah, as they are not game.
Analogy: turtle resembles beetles and lizards.
3
Second rationale: not meeting the definition of game
Game animals are those that require trickery to catch and are intentionally hunted. Turtles can be caught easily and are not normally targeted, so they are not game.
Penalty applies only to game.
4
Conclusion
Both reasons independently lead to no penalty. The principle is that only game animals trigger fidyah when killed by a muhrim.
No significant ikhtilaf among Hanafis on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ فِي ذَبْحِ السُّلْحَفَاةِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الْهَوَامِ وَالْحَشَرَاتِ فَاشْبَهَ الْخَنَافِسَ وَالْوَزَغَاتِ وَيُمْكِنُ أَخْذُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ حِيْلَةٍ وَكَذَا لا يُقصَدُّ بِالأخْذِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ صَيْدًا. تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کچھوا مار ڈالا تو اس پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پچھواز مین کے کیڑوں مکوڑوں میں سے ہے۔ پس یہ نجاست کے کیڑوں اور چھپکلیوں کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور کیڑے مکوڑوں کو مار ڈالنے میں ضمان نہیں آتا۔ لہذا کچھوے کو مارنے پر بھی ضمان نہ آئے گا۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ کچھوے کو بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑنا ممکن ہے اور کوئی اس کے پکڑنے کا ارادہ بھی نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے یہ شکار کا جانور بھی شمار نہ ہوگا۔ حالانکہ جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے شکار کا جانور مار ڈالنے پر ۔ اس لئے بھی جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔
And there is nothing upon him regarding the slaughter of the turtle, because it is from the harmful insects and crawling creatures, so it resembles beetles and lizards. And it is possible to take it without trickery, and also it is not intended to be taken, so it is not game. Explanation: If a muhrim kills a turtle, no penalty is obligatory upon him. Because the turtle is from the insects and crawling creatures. So it resembles impurity insects and lizards. And killing insects does not incur penalty. Therefore, killing a turtle also does not incur penalty. Secondly, it is possible to catch a turtle without a trick, and no one intends to catch it. Therefore, it will not be considered a game animal. Since penalty is only obligatory for killing a game animal, therefore no penalty will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage clarifies that killing a turtle during ihram carries no penalty (daman). The author gives two reasons. First, the turtle is categorized as a harmful insect or crawling creature (hawamm and hasharat). It is analogous to beetles or lizards, which are not game and whose killing incurs no penalty. Killing ordinary insects is permissible without expiation. Second, the turtle does not meet the definition of game: it can be caught without trickery (hilah), and people do not normally intend to catch it. Game is defined as an animal that requires a trick to catch and is intentionally pursued. Since the turtle fails both conditions, it is not considered game, and therefore the fidyah for killing game does not apply. The Urdu commentary reinforces this: penalty (daman or jaza) is only for game animals, not for insects.

Key Terms
سُلْحَفَاةٌ (sulḥafāh): A turtle or tortoise; considered a crawling creature, not game.
هَوَامّ (hawāmm): Harmful insects or reptiles that creep; they are not considered game and killing them incurs no penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Because turtles are water animals
C) Because turtles are considered harmful insects and can be caught without a trick
D) Because turtles are domesticated

Key Takeaway
A turtle is not game; killing it in ihram carries no penalty because it resembles insects and fails both criteria of game (trickery and intention).

Compensation for Milking Game in the Haram
Ruling on milking game in the Haram with qiyas reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for milking game animals in the Haram, explain the qiyas reasoning that requires compensation of the milk's value, and distinguish this from other forms of harm to game.

Core Idea
You must compensate for what you take from Haram game, even its milk — because every part carries the sanctity of the whole.

In this lesson, we explore a specific ruling from al-Hidayah regarding game animals within the sacred precinct of Makkah. The passage addresses an action short of killing: milking. The Hanafi school holds that taking any part of a protected game animal requires compensation, and the reasoning is based on a clear analogy with harming the whole animal. This ruling illustrates how the sanctity of the Haram extends to every part of the game, and how qiyas (analogy) is used to derive rulings for new cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its context
The act is milking a game animal within the Haram. Note that the Haram has special rulings: game cannot be hunted, harmed, or disturbed. The act of milking is a form of taking a part of the animal.
The ruling does not apply to domestic animals or game outside the Haram.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that the milk's value (qimah) must be paid as compensation (daman). This is wajib (obligatory).
Compensation is monetary, not a fixed fidyah.
3
Analyze the qiyas (analogy)
The reasoning: the asl (original case) is killing or injuring a game animal in the Haram, which requires fidyah. The far' (new case) is milking. The illa (effective cause) is that milk is a part (juz') of the game animal, so harming that part is analogous to harming the whole. Thus, the hukm (compensation) transfers.
The illa is jaliyyah (clear) because the milk is physically part of the animal.
4
Note the practical implication
The compensation is the market value of the milk taken. It is given in charity (or as a form of daman). This ruling ensures that any form of taking from Haram game, even without killing, incurs a penalty.
This differs from some other schools that might require fidyah only for killing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ حَلَبَ صَيْدَ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِ فِيْمَهُ لِأَنَّ اللَّبَنَ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ القَصْيدِ فَاسْبَهَ كُلَّهُ. تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے حرم کے شکار کا دودھ نکالا تو اس پر دودھ کی قیمت بطور ضمان واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ دودھ شکار کے اجزاء میں سے ہے پس دودھ مین شکار کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور شکار میں جزاء واجب ہے تو اس کے جزیعنی دودھ میں بھی واجب ہوگی۔
And whoever milks a game animal of the Haram, upon him is its value, because the milk is from the parts of the game, so it resembles the whole. Explanation: If someone milks a game animal of the Haram, then the value of the milk is obligatory upon him as a guarantee. Because milk is from the parts of the game, so milk resembles the game, and fidyah is obligatory for the game, so for its part (milk) it will also be obligatory.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage rules on milking a game animal within the boundaries of the Haram (the sacred precinct of Makkah). The ruling is that the person must pay the value (qimah) of the milk as compensation (daman). The reasoning is based on analogy (qiyas): milk is a part (juz') of the game animal. Since killing or harming the whole animal incurs fidyah (ransom), similarly taking a part of it, like milk, also requires compensation equal to the value of that part. The Urdu commentary clarifies that this is a form of guarantee (daman) because milk is a component of the game. This ruling applies to game animals that are protected within the Haram; it does not apply to domestic animals. The compensation is not a fixed measure but the market value of the milk taken.

Key Terms
صَيْدُ الْحَرَمِ (ṣayd al-ḥaram): Game animals that are protected within the sacred precinct of Makkah; they cannot be hunted, harmed, or milked without penalty.
قِيمَة (qīmah): Monetary value of the milk, to be given as compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) The milk is a part of the game animal, so harming it is like harming the whole.
C) The act of milking is prohibited in the Haram.
D) The milk must be given to the Kaaba.

Key Takeaway
Milking a game animal in the Haram requires paying the value of the milk as compensation, based on qiyas that milk is a part of the protected animal.

Killing Non-Edible Game: Predators Require Fidyah
Ruling on killing non-edible game like predators; debate with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fidyah for killing non-edible game animals in ihram and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
Fidyah for predators: Hanafi requires it, Shafi'i exempts them as fawasiq.

This passage addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: when a pilgrim in ihram kills a predator (e.g., a wolf or lion) that is not eaten, must he pay fidyah (ransom)? The Hanafi school answers yes, because such animals are considered game and only five specific harmful animals (fawasiq) are exempt. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that all inherently harmful creatures fall under the fawasiq exception and that the word 'kalb' (dog) linguistically covers all predators. The Hanafi response rests on 'urf (custom) and the numeration of the exempted animals.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its exception
Identify the rule: fidyah is obligatory for killing any game animal, including non-edible ones like predators, except those specifically listed by the Shariah (the five fawasiq: crow, kite, scorpion, rat, biting dog).
The list is exhaustive; analogy cannot add to it.
2
Present the Shafi'i objection
Recognize two Shafi'i arguments: (1) predators are created to harm, so they should be included in the fawasiq exception; (2) linguistically, the word 'kalb' (dog) covers all predators, so they are exempt by the hadith on fawasiq.
The Shafi'i position is that no fidyah is required for any harmful animal.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand the Hanafi response: (a) predators are game because they are wild and are sought for hide, hunting, or repelling harm; (b) analogizing to fawasiq would nullify the specific count of the exempted animals; (c) 'urf (custom) does not call a lion or wolf a 'kalb', and 'urf takes precedence over pure linguistic extension.
The Hanafi school prioritizes customary usage over literal linguistic scope.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
Note the practical outcome: if a Hanafi pilgrim kills a wolf, he must pay fidyah; under Shafi'i ruling, no fidyah is due. This affects the pilgrim's obligation and potential compensation.
The difference is a real, applied ruling in hajj rituals.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi position
Within the Hanafi school, the position that fidyah is required for such killings is the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), supported by the authority of al-Hidayah.
No significant intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ قَتَلَ مَالَا يُؤكَلُ لَحْمُهُ مِنَ الصَّيدِ كَالرّسبَاعِ وَنَحْوِهَا فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاءُ إِلَّا مَا اسْتَتْنَاهُ الشَّرْعُ وَهُوَ مَا عَدَدْنَاهُ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعَى لاَ يَجِبُ الْجَزَاءُ لأنَّهَا جُبِلَتْ عَلَى الْإِيْدَاءِ فَدَخَلَتْ فِي الْفَوَاسِقِ الْمُسْتَشَنَاهِ وَكَذَا إِسْم الْكَلْبِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الرِّبَاعَ بِأَسَرِهَا لُغَةٌ وَلَنَا أَنَّ السَّبْعَ صَيْدٌ لِتَوَحْشِهِ وَكَوْنَهُ مَقْصُودَ بِالْأَحَدٍ إِمَّا لِجِلْدِهِ أَوْ لِيُصْطَادَبِهِ أَوْ لِدَفْعِ اذَاهُ وَالْقِيَاسُ عَلَى الْفَوَاسِقِ مُمْتَنِعُ لِمَا فِيهِ مِنْ إِبْطَالِ الْعَدَدِ وَاسْمُ الْكَلْبِ لَا يَقَعُ عَلَى السَّبُعِ عُرُفًا وَالْعَرَفُ أَمْلك
And whoever kills from game that whose flesh is not eaten, like predators and the like, upon him is the fidyah (ransom), except what the Shariah has excluded, and that is what we have enumerated. And al-Shafi'i said: Fidyah is not obligatory, because they are created for harming, so they enter into the excepted harmful animals (fawasiq). Also, the word 'kalb' (dog) linguistically includes all predators. But we (Hanafis) argue: the predator is game because of its wildness and because it is intended for something: either for its hide, or to hunt with it, or to repel its harm. Analogy with the harmful animals (fawasiq) is prevented because it would lead to nullifying the count (of excluded animals). And the word 'kalb' does not apply to predators in common usage ('urf), and 'urf has precedence.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding killing predators (like lions, wolves, etc.) that are not eaten. The Hanafi ruling: fidyah is required for killing any game animal, including non-edible ones like predators, except those specifically exempted by Shariah (the five fawasiq: crow, kite, scorpion, rat, and biting dog). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that no fidyah is required because these animals are inherently harmful (jubilat 'ala al-iydha') and thus fall under the exception of fawasiq. He also argues that the Arabic word 'kalb' (dog) linguistically covers all predators, so they are included in the exception. The Hanafi response: predators are game because they are wild (tawahhush) and are sought for some purpose (hide, hunting with them, or repelling harm). They are not like the specified fawasiq. Analogy to fawasiq is invalid because it would nullify the count of the specifically excluded animals. Furthermore, in common usage ('urf), the word 'kalb' does not refer to predators; it refers specifically to the dog. Since 'urf is authoritative, the linguistic argument fails. Therefore, killing such predators in ihram requires fidyah.

Key Terms
فَوَاسِق (fawāsiq): Harmful animals that are exempt from the prohibition of killing in ihram; specifically five: crow, kite, scorpion, rat, and biting dog.
عُرْف (‘urf): Common usage or custom; here used to determine the meaning of 'kalb' (dog).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is killing a wolf in ihram subject to fidyah despite being harmful?
A) Because wolves are edible
B) Because wolves are not included in the five fawasiq and are considered game
C) Because the word 'kalb' includes wolves
D) Because wolves are domesticated

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, fidyah for killing non-edible game in ihram is wajib unless the animal is one of the five specific fawasiq, and this is upheld against the Shafi'i view by appealing to the fixed count and customary usage.

No Penalty for Killing a Turtle During Ihram
Ruling on killing a turtle during ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a turtle during ihram and explain the two-part reasoning based on its classification as a crawling insect (hawamm) and not game (sawd).

Core Idea
Killing a turtle in ihram incurs no penalty because it is classified as a crawling insect, not game.

In this lesson, we examine a specific ruling from the Hanafi school regarding a muhrim (one in ihram) who kills a turtle. The passage explains why no compensation (daman or jaza') is due. We will explore the legal reasoning, including the analogy to insects and the definition of game (sawd).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is killing a turtle while in the state of ihram. The ruling is that no penalty (daman/jaza') is obligatory upon the muhrim.
2
Examine the first reason: classification as hawamm
The passage states that the turtle is among the hawamm (crawling insects) and hasharat (vermin), like beetles and geckos. Since killing such creatures incurs no penalty, the same applies to turtles.
This is an implicit analogy (qiyas khafi).
3
Examine the second reason: not considered game (sawd)
The turtle is not typically hunted or intended for capture; it can be caught without a trick (hilah). Therefore, it does not fall under the category of sawd, which is subject to penalty.
The Urdu commentary emphasizes that no one intends to catch it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ فِي ذَبْحِ السُّلْحَفَاةِ لِأَنَّهُ مِنَ الْهَوَامِ وَالْحَشَرَاتِ فَاشْبَهَ الْخَنَافِسَ وَالْوَزَغَاتِ وَيُمْكِنُ أَخْذُهُ مِنْ غَيْرِ حِيْلَةٍ وَكَذَا لا يُقصَدُّ بِالأخْذِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ صَيْدًا ترجمہ اور محرم پر کچھوا مار ڈالنے میں کچھ واجب نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ کیڑوں مکوڑوں میں سے ہے۔ پس وہ نجاست کے کیڑوں اور چھپکلیوں کے مانند ہو گیا اور بغیر حیلہ کے اس کا پکڑنا بھی ممکن نہیں ہے اور ایسے ہی اس کا پکڑنا بھی مقصود نہیں ہوتا اس لئے وہ شکار نہ ہوا۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کچھوا مار ڈالا تو اس پر کوئی ضمان واجب نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ پچھواز مین کے کیڑوں مکوڑوں میں سے ہے۔ پس یہ نجاست کے کیڑوں اور چھپکلیوں کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ اور کیڑے مکوڑوں کو مار ڈالنے میں ضمان نہیں آتا۔ لہذا کچھوے کو مارنے پر بھی ضمان نہ آئے گا۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ کچھوے کو بغیر حیلہ کے پکڑنا ممکن ہے اور کوئی اس کے پکڑنے کا ارادہ بھی نہیں کرتا۔ اس لئے یہ شکار کا جانور بھی شمار نہ ہوگا۔ حالانکہ جزاء واجب ہوتی ہے شکار کا جانور مار ڈالنے پر ۔ اس لئے بھی جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔
And there is nothing upon him regarding the slaughter of the turtle because it is among the crawling insects and vermin, so it resembles beetles and geckos. And it is possible to catch it without a trick, and likewise it is not intended for catching, so it is not game. Translation: And upon the muhrim, there is no obligation in killing a turtle. Because it is among insects and vermin. So it became like the insects of impurity and geckos. And it is possible to catch it without a trick, and likewise its capture is not intended, so it is not considered game. Explanation of the issue: If a muhrim kills a turtle, no compensation is obligatory upon him. Because it is among the crawling insects. So it resembles the insects of impurity and geckos. And there is no compensation in killing insects and vermin. Therefore, no compensation will be due for killing a turtle. The second point is that the turtle can be caught without a trick, and no one intends to catch it. Therefore, it will not be counted as a game animal. Whereas compensation is obligatory for killing a game animal. Therefore, also no compensation will be obligatory.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hanafi school regarding the killing of a turtle by a person in the state of ihram. The author states that there is no penalty (jaza') or compensation (daman) for killing a turtle. The reasoning is twofold: first, turtles are classified among the hawamm (crawling insects) and hasharat (vermin), which are not considered game (sawd). They are analogized to beetles and geckos, for which there is no penalty. Second, the turtle is not typically hunted or intended for capture; it can be caught without a trick (hilah), meaning it is easily obtainable and not pursued as game. Therefore, it falls outside the category of sawd (huntable game) for which the Quranic penalty applies. The Urdu commentary reinforces this, explaining that since turtles are akin to insects that are not subject to daman, and since no one normally hunts them, no penalty is incurred.

Key Terms
سُلْحَفَاة (sulhafah): Turtle, considered a type of crawling insect in this context.
هَوَام (hawamm): Crawling insects or vermin, such as beetles and geckos.
صَيْد (sawd): Game animals that are hunted and intended for capture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) No penalty is obligatory.
C) The muhrim must give sadaqah.
D) The muhrim's ihram becomes invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that killing a turtle during ihram incurs no penalty because it is classified as a crawling insect (hawamm) and not as game (sawd).

Penalty for Milking a Hunted Animal in the Haram
Ruling on milking a hunted animal in the Haram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on milking a game animal in the Haram and apply the qiyas (analogical reasoning) that derives compensation for a part from the whole.

Core Idea
Milking a game animal in the Haram requires payment of the milk's value, as part is treated like the whole.

The Haram (sanctuary of Makkah) has special sanctity; harming game animals there incurs compensation (jaza'). This lesson extends that principle to a partial taking—milking. By analogy, if killing the whole animal requires a penalty, then taking its milk, being a part, also requires compensation of its market value.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is milking a game animal within the Haram. The ruling is that the person must pay the value (qimah) of the milk as compensation.
2
Recognize the dalil (evidence) structure
The author does not cite a primary textual proof but uses qiyas (analogy). The implicit asl (original case) is killing a game animal in the Haram, which requires a penalty. The far' (new case) is milking it.
The analogy is a qiyas khafi (hidden analogy) because milk is not explicitly mentioned in the primary sources.
3
Analyze the illah (effective cause)
The illah is that milk is a part (juz') of the game animal. Since the whole animal is sacred and harming it incurs compensation, taking a part also incurs compensation proportionally.
The illah is established by the fact that milk originates from the animal and is inseparable from its body.
4
Apply the qiyas to derive the ruling
Just as killing the whole animal requires payment of its value (or a sacrificial animal equivalent), milking it requires payment of the milk's market value. The compensation is wajib (obligatory) as a form of daman (liability).

وَمَنْ حَلَبَ صَيْدَ الْحَرَمِ فَعَلَيْهِ فِيْمَهُ لِأَنَّ اللَّبَنَ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ القَصْيدِ فَاسْبَهَ كُلَّهُ ترجمہ اور جس نے حرم کے شکار کو دوہ لیا تو اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے کیونکہ دودھ شکار کے اجزاء میں سے ہے پس دودھ اسکے کل کے مشابہ ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے حرم کے شکار کا دودھ نکالا تو اس پر دودھ کی قیمت بطور ضمان واجب ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ دودھ شکار کے اجزاء میں سے ہے پس دودھ مین شکار کے مشابہ ہو گیا اور شکار میں جزاء واجب ہے تو اس کے جزیعنی دودھ میں بھی واجب ہوگی۔
And whoever milks a game animal of the Haram, then upon him is its value, because milk is among the parts of the game, so it resembles the whole. Translation: And whoever milks the game of the Haram, then upon him is its value, because milk is among the parts of the game, so milk resembles the whole. Explanation of the issue: The issue is that if someone extracts milk from the game of the Haram, then upon him is the value of the milk as compensation. Because milk is among the parts of the game, so milk resembles the game, and for killing the game a penalty is obligatory, so for its part, i.e., milk, a penalty is also obligatory.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement regarding milking a game animal within the Haram (sanctuary of Makkah). The Hanafi ruling is that one must pay the value (qimah) of the milk as compensation. The reasoning is that milk is a part (juz') of the game animal, and since killing the whole animal incurs a penalty (jaza'), taking a part of it also incurs a proportional penalty. The Urdu commentary explains that just as killing the animal requires compensation, extracting milk, being a part, requires payment of its market value.

Key Terms
حَلَبَ (halaba): To milk an animal actively (by hand).
صَيْدَ الْحَرَمِ (sawd al-haram): Game animals within the boundaries of the Haram (sanctuary of Makkah).
قِيمَة (qimah): Market value (of the milk) to be paid as compensation.

Killing Predators During Ihram: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on penalty for killing non-edible predatory animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing predatory animals during ihram and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the Hanafi response.

Core Idea
Predators are game; killing them in ihram incurs penalty unless they are among the five exempted fawaasiq.

When a muhrim kills a non-edible predatory animal such as a lion or wolf, is a penalty (jaza') obligatory? The Hanafi school says yes, except for five specific animals exempted by the Prophet. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that all harmful animals are automatically exempt. This lesson unpacks the evidence from both sides and explains why the Hanafi school maintains its position based on the definition of game, the specificity of the hadith, and the role of common usage (urf).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: penalty (jaza') is wajib for killing any non-edible predatory animal, except for the five fawaasiq (scorpion, crow, kite, rat, biting dog).
The five fawaasiq are the only exceptions; they are specified in the hadith.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no penalty is due because predators are created for harm (jubilat 'ala al-idha') and thus fall under the exemption of the fawaasiq.
Shafi'i also argues that the word 'kalb' in the hadith linguistically includes all predators.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Shafi'i's two main arguments: (1) qiyas: predators are similar to the fawaasiq in causing harm, so they should be exempt; (2) linguistic: the term 'kalb' (dog) literally covers all predators, so the Prophet's exception of 'al-kalb al-aqur' includes them.
The hadith: 'Five are fawaasiq that may be killed in ihram...' but Shafi'i extends it.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school counters: (1) predators are game (sawd) because they are wild and hunted for skin, training, or harm-repelling; the Quranic prohibition on killing game applies. (2) Qiyas is invalid because it nullifies the specified number (five) in the hadith. (3) In common usage (urf), 'kalb' does not apply to lions or wolves; urf overrides linguistic extension.
The principle: 'al-urf amlak' – custom has stronger authority than literal language in determining meaning.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: a Hanafi muhrim must pay jaza' for killing a wolf, while a Shafi'i muhrim does not. This affects the validity and completeness of the Hajj.
The mufta bihi is the Hanafi position, as supported by the majority and the strength of urf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

لأنَّهَا جُبِلَتْ عَلَى الْإِيْدَاءِ فَدَخَلَتْ فِي الْفَوَاسِقِ الْمُسْتَشَنَاهِ وَكَذَا إِسْم الْكَلْبِ يَتَنَاوَلُ الرِّبَاعَ بِأَسَرِهَا لُغَةٌ وَلَنَا أَنَّ السَّبْعَ صَيْدٌ لِتَوَحْشِهِ کر دیا ہے۔ اور مستثنیٰ وہ ہیں جن کو ہم شمار کر چکے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ جزاء واجب نہیں ہے کیونکہ یہ جانور ایذاء دینے کے لئے پیدا کئے گئے ہیں۔ پس یہ ان فواسق میں داخل ہوں گے جن کو مستثنیٰ کیا گیا And whoever kills what is not eaten of its meat from game, like predators and the like, then upon him is the penalty (jaza'), except what the shariah has excluded, which we have enumerated. And al-Shafi'i said: The penalty is not obligatory because these animals are created for harm, so they enter into the excepted fawaasiq (harmful animals). Also, the name 'kalb' (dog) linguistically includes all predators. And our evidence is that the predator is game due to its wildness and being intended for capture either for its skin, for hunting with it, or for repelling its harm. Qiyas (analogy) to the fawaasiq is invalid because it would nullify the number (of excepted animals). And the name 'kalb' is not applied to predators in common usage ('urf), and 'urf is stronger. Translation: And whoever kills an animal whose meat is not eaten, like predators and the like, then penalty is obligatory upon him, except what shariah has excluded, and the excluded are those we have counted. And Imam Shafi'i said that penalty is not obligatory because these animals are created for harm, so they enter into the excepted fawaasiq. Also, the word 'kalb' linguistically includes all predators. Our evidence is that the predator is game because it is wild and is intended for capture: either for its skin (like lions), or to hunt with it (like cheetahs), or to repel its harm (like wild boars). So these characteristics make it game, and the Quranic verse 'And do not kill game while you are in ihram' (5:95) applies. Therefore, killing them incurs penalty. The response to Shafi'i's qiyas is that analogizing predators to the fawaasiq is invalid because it would nullify the specified number (five) mentioned in the hadith. And Shafi'i's claim that the word 'kalb' applies to predators is wrong because in 'urf it does not apply; 'urf is stronger. Therefore, predators are not included in the exception, and killing them requires penalty.
Source pages p. 466

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the penalty for killing non-edible predatory animals (like lions, cheetahs, wolves) during ihram. The Hanafi position is that a penalty (jaza') is wajib for killing such animals, except for the five fawaasiq (harmful animals) specifically exempted by the Prophet (scorpion, crow, kite, rat, and biting dog). Imam al-Shafi'i argues that no penalty is required because these animals are inherently harmful and thus included in the exception, and the linguistic meaning of 'kalb' encompasses all predators. The Hanafi response, as presented in the text, is that predators are considered game (sawd) because they are wild, are hunted for skin or training, or for repelling harm; therefore, the general prohibition on killing game applies. Analogizing them to the fawaasiq is rejected because it would contradict the specific enumeration of five animals in the hadith, and in common usage ('urf) the term 'kalb' does not apply to predators like lions. Hence, killing them requires penalty. The Urdu commentary elaborates on the characteristics that make an animal game and emphasizes that 'urf is the stronger determinant over linguistic extension.

Key Terms
الْجَزَاء (jaza'): The penalty or compensation for killing game during ihram, typically a sacrificial animal or its value.
السَّبُع (sabu'): Predatory animal, such as lion, leopard, wolf.
الْفَوَاسِق (fawaasiq): The five harmful animals exempted from hunting prohibition: scorpion, crow, kite, rat, and biting dog.
الْعُرْف (urf): Customary usage (in language); here, it is used to argue that 'kalb' does not apply to predators in common speech.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) A crow

Key Takeaway
Killing a non-edible predator during ihram incurs a penalty because it is considered game, except for the five fawaasiq specifically exempted by the Prophet.
