Penalty Value Not Exceeding a Sheep (Intra-Hanafi Dispute)
Ruling on maximum value of penalty for non-edible animals and dispute with Zufar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the maximum penalty for non-edible game animals and evaluate Imam Zufar's alternative view using the hadith of the hyena.

Core Idea
The penalty for non-edible game is capped at a sheep's value, based on the hadith of the hyena, not full market value.

A muhrim who kills a non-edible predatory animal (like a hyena) incurs a penalty (jaza'). But what is the measure? Does it follow the animal's market value, or is there a fixed limit? The Hanafi school holds that the penalty cannot exceed the value of a sheep, drawing on a specific prophetic ruling. This lesson examines the evidence and an intra-Hanafi objection raised by Imam Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the dispute
What is the act in question? Killing a non-edible game animal during ihram. The dispute: is the penalty the full market value (Zufar) or capped at the value of a sheep (majority)?
The animal is non-edible, e.g., hyena, wolf.
2
State the majority Hanafi position and its proof
The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that the penalty does not exceed a sheep. Their dalil is the hadith: 'The hyena is game, and in it is a sheep.'
The hadith is a specific text (nass) for the hyena, and it is extended to all similar non-edible game animals via analogy (qiyas) based on common 'illa (benefit of skin, not harm).
3
State Zufar's position and his proof
Imam Zufar holds that the full market value is wajib, analogizing non-edible animals to edible game animals (ma'kul al-lahm) where the penalty is based on value.
For edible game, the penalty is the value of the animal (e.g., a deer). Zufar sees no distinction.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to Zufar
The Hanafi response rejects the analogy: the value of non-edible animals is considered only for the benefit of their skin, not because they are harmful aggressors. Hence, the cap from the hadith applies.
The 'illa for the cap is that the animal is not valued as food, so a fixed maximum (sheep) suffices.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is the majority view: penalty is capped at the value of a sheep. In practice, the muhrim pays up to the value of a sheep, not the animal's full market price.
If the animal is worth more than a sheep, the penalty is still only a sheep's value.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا يُجَاوِرُ بِقِيمَتِهِ شَاةً وَ قَالَ زُفُرْ يَجِبُ بَالِغَةً مَّا بَلَغَتْ إِعْتِبَارًا بِمَا كُولِ اللَّحْمِ وَلَنَا قُولُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الضبع ضيدٌ وَفِيْهِ الشَّاةَ وَلِأَنَّ اِعْتِبَارَ قِيْمَتِهِ لِمَكَانِ الْانْتِفَاعِ بِجِلْدِهِ لاَ لأَنَّهُ مُحَارِبُ مُؤذِى وَمِنْ هَذَا الْوَجْهِ لَا يُزَادُ عَلَى قِيمَةِ الشَّاةِ ظَاهِرًا ترجمہ اور اس کی قیمت سے بکری کی قیمت نہ بڑھائی جائے گی ۔ اور امام زفر نے کہا کہ پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی جہاں تک پہنچے ماکول اللحم پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ بجو شکار ہے اور اس میں بکری واجب ہے۔ اور اس لئے کہ اس کی قیمت اس کی کھال سے نفع اٹھانے کے اعتبار سے ہے نہ اس لئے کہ وہ جنگجو موذی ہے اور اس وجہ سے بظاہر بکری کی قیمت سے نہ کی اس کیسے اعتبار نہ کہ ہ اور سے کی سے نہ بڑھے گی۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ محرم نے اگر غیر ماکول اهم درندہ کوقتل کر دیا تو اس پر بطور جزاء اس قدر واجب کیا جائے کہ وہ ایک بکری کی قیمت سے تجاوز نہ کرے۔ امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ مقتول درندہ کی پوری قیمت واجب ہوگی خواہ کتنی ہی ہو۔ امام زفر غیر ما کول کو ماکول اللحم پر قیاس کرتے ہیں۔ اور ہماری دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول الصَّبعُ صَيْدُ وَفِيهِ شَاه - دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ غیر ماکول الہم کی قیمت کا
And its value should not exceed a sheep. And Zufar said: It is obligatory (to pay) whatever value it reaches, by analogy to edible meat animals. And we have the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'The hyena is game, and in it (as penalty) is a sheep.' And because its value is considered for the benefit of its skin, not because it is a harmful aggressor. From this aspect, it is not increased beyond the value of a sheep apparently. Translation: And its value shall not exceed the value of a sheep. And Imam Zufar said that the full value is obligatory whatever it reaches, drawing analogy to edible meat animals. Our evidence is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The hyena is game, and in it is a sheep.' And because its value is considered for the benefit of its skin, not because it is a harmful aggressor. For this reason, apparently it is not increased beyond the value of a sheep. Explanation: If a muhrim kills a non-edible predatory animal, then as a penalty such an amount is obligatory that does not exceed the value of one sheep. Imam Zufar said that the full value of the killed predator is obligatory, no matter how much it is. Imam Zufar analogizes non-edible animals to edible ones. Our evidence is the statement of the Prophet: 'The hyena is game, and in it is a sheep.' The second evidence is that the value of non-edible meat ... (incomplete).
Source pages p. 467

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the amount of penalty for killing a non-edible game animal (like a hyena or other predatory animal). The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that the penalty should not exceed the value of a sheep (shah). This is based on the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that a hyena is considered game and its penalty is a sheep. The reasoning is that the value of such animals is primarily for their skin, not because they are harmful, so the penalty should be capped at the value of a sheep. Imam Zufar argues that the full market value should be paid, analogizing non-edible animals to edible meat animals (ma'kul al-lahm) where the penalty is based on the animal's value. The Hanafi response rejects this analogy, maintaining the specific hadith ruling for the hyena as a precedent for all similar animals. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the penalty for non-edible predatory animals should not exceed the value of a sheep, countering Zufar's view.

Key Terms
شَاة (shah): A sheep or goat (the animal used as a standard for the penalty value).
الضَّبَع (dabu'): Hyena, a non-edible predatory animal used as an example in the hadith.
ما يُؤكَلُ لَحْمُهُ (ma yu'kalu lahmuhu): Edible meat animals (e.g., deer, rabbit). Zufar analogizes non-edible to these.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The full market value of the animal.
B) The value of a sheep.
C) A camel.
D) Nothing, as it is not game.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school caps the penalty for non-edible game at the value of a sheep, based on the hadith of the hyena and the 'illa of skin benefit.

Killing a Predatory Animal in Ihram: The Hanafi Position on Compensation
States ruling on killing predatory animals and rebuts Shafi'i's view

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on killing a non-edible predatory animal in ihram, explain the Hanafi definition of sayd, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on the five fawasiq and the word 'kalb'.

Core Idea
A predator is sayd; killing it in ihram requires compensation—only five fawasiq are exempt.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does killing a lion or cheetah in ihram incur compensation? The Hanafi school says yes, based on the Quranic prohibition of killing game and a definition of sayd that includes predatory animals. The Shafi'i school argues they are like the five noxious animals (fawasiq) that are exempt. Let us examine the arguments and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that killing any non-edible predatory animal (e.g., lion, cheetah, wolf) in ihram incurs wajib compensation (jaza'). These animals are considered sayd (game) under the general prohibition of Quran 5:95.
The compensation amount is specified separately (value up to a goat).
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that no compensation is required for such animals. He argues that their harmful nature places them among the five fawasiq (noxious animals) which are explicitly exempt from compensation.
The five fawasiq are: crow, kite, scorpion, snake, and vicious dog.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Shafi'i's proof: (a) These animals are harmful, so they are like the fawasiq by analogy. (b) The hadith excepting 'kalb 'aqur' (vicious dog) is extended to all harmful predators because they share the 'illa (cause) of harmfulness.
The hadith: 'Five are fawasiq and may be killed in ihram...'
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: (a) Analogizing to the fawasiq is invalid because it would nullify the specific count (only five are excepted). (b) The word 'kalb' (dog) does not customarily apply to lions, cheetahs, etc. Custom ('urf) is a strong legal principle and cannot be overridden by a weak analogy.
Hanafi usul holds that 'urf is a valid source of law when texts are ambiguous.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: Under Shafi'i law, a pilgrim can kill a lion without paying anything. Under Hanafi law, compensation wajib (value up to a goat). This difference affects pilgrimage expenses and the concept of game prohibition.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is the Hanafi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Predatory animals are included. And our proof is that a predatory animal is game (sayd) because it is wild and is intended to be caught, either for its skin, or to play with it for hunting, or to repel its harm. And analogy to the five fawasiq (noxious animals) is invalid because it would nullify the specific count, and the word 'kalb' (dog) is not customarily applied to a predatory animal, and custom is the stronger principle. Explanation of the issue: If a muhrim kills a non-edible game animal, such as predatory animals like lion, cheetah, etc., then compensation (jaza') is due on him. Yes, those animals which the Shari'ah has excepted, i.e., the five fawasiq whose count was previously given, are not subject to compensation. Imam Shafi'i says that killing non-edible game does not incur compensation. His proof is that these predatory animals have a nature of causing harm, so they are included among the fawasiq which are excepted from compensation. Also, the Messenger of Allah excepted 'kalb 'aqur' (the vicious dog). Our proof is that predatory animals are wild, flee from people, and people intend to catch them, either to benefit from their skin like the lion, or to use them in hunting like the cheetah, or to repel their harm like the wild boar. So any animal with these characteristics is called game (sayd). Therefore, predatory animals are called game. And concerning game, Allah says: {Do not kill game while you are in the state of ihram}. So killing them incurs compensation. The response to Imam Shafi'i's analogy is that analogizing predatory animals to the fawasiq is invalid because it would nullify the specific count mentioned in the hadith (of Shams [?]). Also, his claim that the word 'kalb' applies to predatory animals is incorrect because in custom 'kalb' does not apply to predatory animals, and custom is strong. Therefore, considering them included in the word 'kalb' and exempting them from compensation is not valid; rather, killing them incurs compensation.

Commentary
This passage presents the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim (person in ihram) killing a non-edible predatory animal (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm). It begins by asserting that such animals are considered 'sayd' (game) in Hanafi law, contrary to the view of Imam Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof is based on the Quranic verse prohibiting the killing of game in ihram and the fact that these animals are hunted for skin, sport, or to repel harm—all characteristics of game. The passage then explains the Shafi'i view that these animals are like the five fawasiq (noxious animals) which are exempt from compensation, and that the hadith about 'kalb 'aqur' (vicious dog) covers them. The Hanafi response refutes this: the five fawasiq are specifically enumerated in hadith, so analogizing other animals to them would nullify that specific count. Additionally, the word 'kalb' in 'urf (custom) does not apply to predatory animals like lions and cheetahs; custom is a strong legal principle. Thus, the Hanafi position is that compensation (jaza') is due for killing any such animal, whether edible or not, unless specifically excepted by the Shari'ah. The teacher should note that this ruling is part of the broader discussion on violations of ihram and demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on 'urf and strict adherence to the specific textual exceptions (the five fawasiq).

Key Terms
صید (sayd): Any wild animal that people intend to catch for skin, sport, or to repel harm.
محرم (muhrim): A person who has entered the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah.
جزاء (jaza'): Monetary compensation or an animal sacrifice required for violating the prohibition of killing game in ihram.
فواسق (fawasiq): The five noxious animals (crow, kite, scorpion, snake, vicious dog) that a muhrim may kill without compensation.
کلب عقور (kalb 'aqur): A vicious dog that is harmful and can be killed by a muhrim without compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The muhrim must sacrifice a camel.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a muhrim must pay compensation for killing any non-edible predatory animal in ihram, as only the five specified fawasiq are exempt.

Compensation for Non-Edible Predator: Cap of a Goat's Value
Specifies maximum compensation for killing a non-edible predator and rebuts Imam Zufar's view of full value.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for killing a non-edible predatory animal in ihram and explain why it is capped at a goat's value, citing the hadith and the reasoning based on skin benefit.

Core Idea
Compensation for a non-edible predator is capped at a goat’s value — the hadith overrides qiyas.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the Hajj chapter: the compensation (jaza') for a muhrim who kills a non-edible predatory animal. The Hanafi school limits this compensation to the value of one goat, even if the animal is large and valuable. We will explore the proof from a hadith about the hyena, the reasoning based on skin benefit, and the disagreement of Imam Zufar, who argued for full value by qiyas. Understanding this ruling illustrates how textual evidence (nass) takes precedence over analogy in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a muhrim killing a non-edible predatory animal (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm). The Hanafi ruling is that compensation (wajib) must not exceed the value of one goat.
The ruling applies to animals like lions, wolves, hyenas – any predator whose meat is not consumed.
2
State Imam Zufar's opposing view
Imam Zufar, within the Hanafi school, holds that full market value is wajib, analogizing to edible game animals where compensation equals full value.
His qiyas is based on the common illa of 'being game' (sayd).
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof: the hadith
The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'Al-dhab'u saydun wa fihi shaat' (The hyena is game, and for it a goat is due). This hadith directly specifies a fixed compensation for a specific non-edible predator, setting a precedent for all similar animals.
This is a dalil naqli (textual proof) that is specific (khass) and overrides general qiyas.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof: reasoning about skin benefit
Non-edible animals have value only for their skin (since meat is not eaten). The skin of even large predators typically does not exceed the value of a goat. Therefore, the compensation is capped accordingly.
This reasoning (ta'lil) explains why the hadith's limit is rational and not arbitrary.
5
Conclude with tarjih
The majority of Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) adopt the hadith-based view. Imam Zufar's qiyas is rejected because the explicit text takes priority. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that compensation does not exceed a goat's value.
This tarjih is recorded by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Commentary
This passage addresses the amount of compensation (jaza') for a muhrim who kills a non-edible predatory animal (ghayr ma'kul al-lahm). The Hanafi ruling is that the compensation must not exceed the value of one goat (shaat). The text presents the view of Imam Zufar, who argues for the full market value of the animal, analogizing to edible game (where compensation equals the full value). The Hanafi response relies on two proofs: first, a hadith where the Prophet ruled that a hyena (which is non-edible) requires only a goat, not full value, thus setting a precedent. Second, reasoning: the value of such animals is derived only from their skin (since meat is not consumed), and the skin of even large predators like lions is typically not worth more than a goat in the local market (based on 'urf). Thus, the compensation is capped at one goat's value. This ruling is an example of Hanafi istihsan (juristic preference) over strict qiyas, which would demand full value. The teacher should emphasize that this is a specific application where a textual proof (hadith) overrides analogy, demonstrating the hierarchy of evidence in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
شاة (shaat): A goat or sheep (the standard unit of compensation in many cases).
قيمة (qimah): Market value of the animal.
ضبع (dhab'): Hyena, a non-edible predatory animal used as a precedent.

Key Takeaway
Compensation for killing a non-edible predator in ihram is capped at the value of a goat, based on the hyena hadith and the principle that value is only for the skin.

Killing a Predator in Self-Defense During Ihram
Ruling: muhrim kills predator in self-defense; no compensation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim killing a predator in self-defense and explain why no compensation is due, distinguishing it from killing an owned animal.

Core Idea
Self-defense against a predator waives compensation because Allah's permission overrides His right.

This lesson addresses a specific scenario during ihram: a predatory animal attacks a muhrim and he kills it in self-defense. The Hanafi school rules that no compensation (jaza') is required, even though killing land animals normally incurs a penalty. We will examine the proof from the action of Caliph 'Umar, the counter-argument by Imam Zufar based on analogy to a domestic animal, and the legal principle that distinguishes between rights of Allah and rights of humans.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and the Dispute
Read the first part of the passage: the Hanafi position is that no compensation is due. Note that Imam Zufar dissents, arguing by qiyas to an attacking camel. Understand the question at stake.
2
Analyze the Hanafi Proof from 'Umar
Examine the report: 'Umar killed a predator and sent a goat as a gift, explaining that he had initiated the attack. This implies that if the predator had attacked first, no compensation would be due. Identify how this precedent supports the ruling.
The phrase 'we initiated' indicates compensation is only due when the muhrim starts the aggression.
3
Understand the Legal Principle: Permission Waives Right
The Hanafi response argues that since the Shari'ah permits repelling harm (daf' al-adha), the compensation—a right of Allah—is waived. Compare this to a camel attack: the owner has not given permission, so the killer must pay its value.
The distinction is between haqq Allah (waivable by Shari'ah permission) and haqq al-'abd (requires owner's consent).
4
Evaluate Imam Zufar's Qiyas and the Hanafi Rebuttal
Zufar analogizes the predator to an owned camel: both attack, both are killed, so compensation should be due. The Hanafi rebuttal: the camel is owned; the predator is not. Thus the analogy fails because the permission structure is different.
The key difference is ownership, not the act of killing in self-defense.
5
Synthesize the Ruling and Its Application
Conclude that the mufta bihi position is no compensation. Apply the reasoning: a muhrim defending himself against a wild animal is fulfilling the purpose of self-preservation, with explicit divine permission, so no penalty attaches.
This is an exception to the general rule that killing land animals in ihram requires compensation.

درندے نے محرم پر حملہ کیا محرم نے اسے قتل کر دیا محرم پر کچھ لازم نہیں وَإِذَا صَالَ السَّبُعُ عَلَى الْمُحْرِهِ فَقَتَلَهُ لَا شَيْ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ زُفْرُ يَجِبُ اِعْتِبَارًا بِالْجَمَلِ الصَّائِلِ وَلَنَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عُمَرَ أَنَّهُ قَتَلَ سَبْعًا وَأَهْدَى كَبْشًا وَقَالَ إِنَّا ابتدأنَاهُ وَلِأَنَّ الْمُحْرِمَ مَمْنُوعٌ عَنِ التَّعْرِيضِ لَا عَنْ دَفْعِ الأذى وَاهِذَا كَانَ مَا ذُونَا فِي الْجَمَلِ الصَّائِلِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا إِذْنَ لَهُ مِنَ صَاحِبِ الحَقِّ وَهُوَ العبد ترجمہ اور جب درندہ نے محرم پر حملہ کیا پس محرم نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو محرم پر کچھ واجب نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا ہے کہ واجب ہے حملہ آور اونٹ پر قیاس کرتے ہوئے ۔ ہماری دلیل وہ اثر ہے جو حضرت عمرؓ سے روایت کیا گیا ہے کہ حضرت عمر نے ایک درندہ کو قتل کیا اور بکری بدی بھیجی۔ اور فرمایا کہ ہم نے درندہ پر پہل کی تھی ۔ اور اس لئے کہ محرم کو تعرض کرنے سے روکا گیا ہے نہ کہ اذیت دور کرنے سے اور اسی وجہ سے محرم کو اجازت ہے ایسے جانور کو دفع کرنے کی جس سے اذیت کا تو ہم جو ۔ جیسے فواسق میں ہے۔ پس ان جانوروں کو دفع کرنے کی اجازت بدرجہ اولی ہوگی جن سے اذیت متحقق ہو۔ اور شارع کی طرف سے اجازت کے باوجود حق شارع جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی برخلاف حملہ آور اونٹ کے، کیونکہ قاتل کو صاحب حق کی طرف سے اجازت نہیں ہے اور صاحب حق بندہ ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر درندہ نے محرم پر حملہ کیا اور محرم نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل قیاس ہے یعنی اگر کسی انسان پر اونٹ حملہ آور ہوا پھر اس انسان نے اونٹ کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہے۔ اگر چہ اس نے اپنے اوپر سے دفع کرنے کے لئے اس کو قتل کیا ہے۔ اسی طرح درندہ کو قتل کرنے کی صورت میں بھی قاتل پر جزاء واجب ہو گی۔ ہماری دلیل حضرت عمر کا اثر ہے کہ فاروق اعظم نے ایک درندہ کوقتل کیا اور ایک بکر ابطور ہدی بھیجا اورفرمایا کہ ہم نے درندہ پر پہل کی تھی یعنی اگر ہم پہل کر کے اس کو قتل نہ کرتے بلکہ وہی حملہ کرتا تو ہم پر ہدی کا بکر اواجب نہ ہوتا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ محرم کو جانوروں کے ساتھ تعرض کرنے سے روکا گیا ہے اپنے اوپر سے اذیت دفع کرنے سے نہیں روکا گیا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ فواسق جانوروں میں اذیت موہوم ہے لیکن اس موہوم اذیت کو دور کرنے کی اجازت دی گئی ہے۔ پس درندوں کی اذیت جو تحقیق ہے اس کو دور کرنے کی اجازت بدرجہ اولی ہوگی اور چونکہ درندوں کی اذیت دور کرنے کی اجازت شارع کی جانب سے ہے اس لئے درندہ کے قتل ہونے کی صورت میں شارع کا حق بن کر جزاء واجب نہ ہوگی۔ برخلاف حملہ آور اونٹ کے، کیونکہ حملہ آور اونٹ کو قتل کرنے کی صورت میں قاتل پر اس کی قیمت واجب ہوتی ہے کیونکہ مالک کی طرف سے اس کو قتل کرنے کی کوئی اجازت نہیں ہے۔ پس جب مالک کی طرف سے اجازت نہیں تو مالک کا حق بھی ساقط نہ ہوگا۔
When a predatory animal attacks a muhrim and he kills it, nothing is due on him. Imam Zufar said: it is due, by analogy to an attacking camel. And our proof is the narration from 'Umar that he killed a predatory animal and sent a goat as a gift, and said: 'We initiated (the attack)'. And because the muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm, not from repelling harm. Therefore, he is allowed to repel even imagined harm, as in the case of the fawasiq. So it is more appropriate that he is allowed to repel certain harm. And when there is permission from the Shari'ah, the compensation (as a right of Allah) is not due, unlike the attacking camel, because there is no permission from the owner (of the camel), and the owner is a human. Translation: When a predatory animal attacks a muhrim and he kills it, nothing is due on him. Imam Zufar said it is due, analogizing to an attacking camel. Our proof is the effect narrated from 'Umar: he killed a predatory animal and sent a goat as a gift, and said, 'We initiated (the attack).' And because the muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm, not from repelling harm. Therefore, he is allowed to repel even imagined harm, as in the fawasiq. So it is more appropriate for actual harm. And with permission from the Shari'ah, the compensation as a right of Allah is not due, unlike the attacking camel, because the killer does not have permission from the owner, and the owner is a human. Commentary: If a predatory animal attacks a muhrim and he kills it, no compensation is due. Imam Zufar argues by qiyas: if a camel attacks a person and he kills it, he must pay its value; similarly, killing a predator should incur compensation. Our proof is the report from 'Umar: he killed a predatory animal and sent a goat as a gift, indicating that if he had not initiated the attack, no compensation would be due because it was self-defense. Second, the muhrim is forbidden from initiating aggression, not from repelling harm. Since the Shari'ah permits repelling harm even from imaginary threats (like the fawasiq), it is even more so for actual harm. Therefore, with such permission, the compensation (which is a right of Allah) is not due. This differs from an attacking camel, where the camel is owned by someone and the owner has not given permission for its killing, so the killer must pay its value.
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage deals with a specific case: a predatory animal attacks a muhrim, and the muhrim kills it in self-defense. The Hanafi ruling is that no compensation (jaza') is due. Imam Zufar holds that compensation is wajib, analogizing to a domestic animal (camel) that attacks a person—in that case, the person must pay the owner's value. The Hanafi refutation is based on two arguments: first, the precedent of 'Umar, who killed a predator and sent a goat as a gift, explaining that he had initiated the attack (meaning if the predator had attacked first, he would not have owed anything). Second, the principle that the muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm but not from defending himself. Since the Shari'ah already permits killing the five fawasiq (which cause potential harm) without compensation, it is even more justified to kill an animal causing certain harm. Since the Shari'ah explicitly permits this, the compensation (which is a right of Allah) is waived. This is contrasted with the case of an attacking camel owned by a human: there, the owner has not granted permission to kill his property, so the killer must pay its value. The teacher should highlight the distinction between rights of Allah (which can be waived by divine permission) and rights of humans (which require explicit permission).

Key Terms
صال (saal): Attacking or assaulting (used for animals that charge at a person).
تعرض (ta'arrad): Aggression or initiating harm.
حق الله (haqq Allah): A right belonging to Allah, which can be waived by His permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim is attacked by a lion and kills it in self-defense, what is the Hanafi ruling?
A) The muhrim must pay compensation equal to the lion's value.
B) The muhrim must sacrifice a goat as compensation.
C) No compensation is required because the Shari'ah permits repelling harm.
D) The muhrim's ihram becomes invalid and he must start over.

Key Takeaway
A muhrim who kills a predator in self-defense owes no compensation, as the Shari'ah's permission waives the right of Allah, unlike killing an owned animal where the owner's permission is absent.

Ruling on a Muhrim Killing an Attacking Predator
Hanafi ruling with proof for no compensation when predator attacks

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim killing an attacking predator, identify the proof from 'Umar's precedent, and distinguish the majority view from Imam Zufar's qiyas argument.

Core Idea
No compensation required when a muhrim kills a predator in self-defense; the Lawgiver permits repelling harm.

A muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm to game animals, but not from defending himself. When a predator attacks, the muhrim may kill it without owing any compensation. This lesson examines the Hanafi proof for this ruling and the dispute with Imam Zufar, who analogizes it to an attacking camel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is a muhrim killing a predator that attacks him. The ruling: no compensation (jaza') is due.
This is the majority Hanafi position.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Zufar holds that compensation is wajib by analogy with an attacking camel (a case of property damage).
Zufar's view is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Examine the Hanafi main proof
The hadith of 'Umar: he killed a predator and sacrificed a ram, saying 'We initiated [the attack]' – implying that if the predator had initiated, no sacrifice would be required.
This dalil is ahad but its meaning is clear (qati' al-dalala).
4
Understand the legal principle
The muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm (ta'arruḍ), not from repelling harm (daf' al-adha). Since the Lawgiver permits repelling even imagined harm from fawasiq, repelling actual harm from a predator is a fortiori permissible.
This is based on the principle of al-idhn min al-shar'.
5
Distinguish from the camel analogy
The camel is owned property; the owner has not given permission to kill it, so compensation is due to the owner. A predator is not property, and the Lawgiver has granted permission to kill in self-defense, so no compensation is owed.
The difference is the presence or absence of permission from the right-holder.

When a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, there is nothing upon him. Zufr said: It is obligatory, by analogy with the attacking camel. And for us [Hanafis] is a narration from 'Umar that he killed a predator and sacrificed a ram, saying: 'We initiated [the attack].' And because the muhrim is prohibited from initiating harm, not from repelling harm. And this is more appropriate in repelling imagined harm, as in the case of fawasiq (noxious animals), so it is more appropriate in repelling actual harm. And with the permission from the Lawgiver, the compensation is not obligatory as a right of His, contrary to the attacking camel, because there is no permission from the owner of the right, and the owner is a slave [i.e., a human].
Source pages p. 468

Commentary
This passage addresses a dispute within the Hanafi school: If a predator attacks a muhrim and the muhrim kills it, is compensation required? Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) says yes, by analogy to an attacking camel (which is property). The majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) says no. They rely on the precedent of 'Umar ibn al-Khattab (RA) who killed a predator and voluntarily offered a ram, explicitly noting that if the predator had initiated the attack, no compensation would be required. The reasoning: A muhrim is prohibited from initiating aggression against game, but not from defending himself. Since the Lawgiver permits repelling even imagined harm from fawasiq (like crows, rats, etc.), it is all the more permissible to repel actual harm from a predator. With the Lawgiver's permission, no compensation is owed. This differs from an attacking camel because a camel is owned property; the owner has not given permission to kill it, so the killer must compensate the owner.

Key Terms
السَّبُع (al-sabu'): Predatory animal such as a lion, tiger, wolf, etc. that attacks.
الْمُحْرِم (al-muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for Hajj or Umrah, subject to certain prohibitions.
الْجَزَاء (al-jaza'): Compensation or penalty due for violation of ihram prohibitions, typically an animal sacrifice.
الفَوَاسِق (al-fawasiq): Noxious animals that are permissible to kill even in ihram, such as crows, rats, scorpions, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a predator attacks a muhrim and he kills it, what is required?
A) Compensation (jaza') is obligatory
B) No compensation is required
C) A ram must be sacrificed
D) Fasting is required

Key Takeaway
When a predator attacks a muhrim, no compensation is required because the muhrim is permitted to repel harm, and the Lawgiver's permission waives any right to compensation.

Killing Game Under Duress: Compensation Still Due
Hanafi ruling with proof from Quranic analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a muhrim who kills game under duress must pay compensation, and explain the proof using the Quranic principle of permission coupled with kaffarah.

Core Idea
Necessity permits killing game in ihram but does not waive compulsory compensation.

It is a common misconception that necessity (idtirar) makes a prohibited act not only permissible but also free of any penalty. The Hanafi school, however, maintains that in the state of ihram, the permission granted for violations under duress is always linked to an obligatory expiation. This lesson unpacks that ruling, its proof from the Quran, and its practical implications for pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a muhrim killing game (sayd) when compelled by necessity such as severe hunger. The ruling is that compensation (jaza') is wajib upon him.
2
Identify the operative condition
The condition that triggers the permissibility is idtirar (compulsion/necessity). Without it, the act would be haram. But even with it, compensation is not waived.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is a Quranic principle derived from verse 2:196, where permission to shave the head during ihram due to illness or harm is coupled with fidyah (expiation). The same structure applies here.
4
Explain the wajh al-dalalah
The verse shows that when Allah permits an otherwise prohibited act in ihram, He requires compensation. The imperative for compensation (ففدية) indicates obligation. By analogy, killing game when compelled is permitted but compensation is wajib.
The dalala is qati' because the command for fidyah is explicit and the principle is drawn by qiyas jali.
5
Note the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is that compensation is due in all cases of killing game in ihram, whether voluntary or compelled. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
Some later Hanafis disputed the exact amount, not the principle.

وَإنِ اضْطَرَّ الْمُحْرِمُ إلى قَتْلِ صَيدٍ فَقَتَلَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاء لِأَنَّ الْإِذَنَ مُقَيدُ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ بِالنَّصِ عَلَى مَا تَلَوْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ
ترجمہ اور اگرمحرم کسی شکار کوقتل کرنے کے لئے مجبور ہو۔ پس اس نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر جزا ء واجب ہے کیونکہ اجازت نص کی وجہ سے کفارہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے چنانچہ ہم پہلے تلاوت کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم شدت بھوک وغیرہ کی وجہ سے شکار کوقتل کرنے کی طرف مضطر اور مجبور ہوا۔ چنانچہ اس نے شکار کو مارڈالا تو اس پر بھی جزاء واجب ہے کیونکہ شریعت نے احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے اگر کسی ممنوع کام کو کرنے کی اجازت دی ہے تو وہ اجازت کفارہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنكُمْ مَرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِنْ صَيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نسک ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ضرورت کے وقت سر منڈانے کی اجازت دی ہے مگر فدیہ کفارہ کے ساتھ ۔ پس اسی طرح مضطر کو بھی ضرورت کے وقت شکار ذبح کر کے کھانا جائز ہے مگر بشرط کفارہ اور شکار کا کفارہ اس کی جزاء ہے جس کی تفصیل سابق میں گذر چکی۔
And if the muhrim is compelled to kill game, and he kills it, then the compensation is upon him, because the permission is restricted with expiation by the text as we recited before.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage states that even if a muhrim is compelled by extreme necessity (e.g., severe hunger) to kill game, he still owes the compensation (jaza'). The reason is that the Lawgiver's permission to violate ihram prohibitions under duress is always coupled with the requirement of expiation. The commentator cites the Qur'anic verse about shaving the head due to illness or harm (Quran 2:196), where Allah permits shaving but requires fidyah. Similarly, killing game for food is permitted only with compensation. This underscores the general principle: necessity does not nullify the obligation of kaffarah for violations of ihram.

Key Terms
اضْطَرَّ (idtara): To be compelled or forced by necessity, such as extreme hunger.
الْكَفَّارَة (al-kaffarah): Expiation or compensation for violating a prohibition, often a sacrifice or fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible without any compensation
B) It is permissible but compensation (jaza') is required
C) It is not permissible under any circumstances
D) He must fast instead of compensation

Key Takeaway
A muhrim who kills game under duress must still pay compensation, because permission in ihram is always tied to expiation.

Permissible Animals for a Muhrim to Slaughter
List of domestic animals a muhrim may slaughter without penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which animals a muhrim may slaughter and apply the criterion of domesticity to determine permissibility.

Core Idea
A muhrim may slaughter any domestic animal, but never game (sayd).

When a person enters ihram, certain prohibitions apply, including hunting wild game. However, slaughtering domestic animals for food remains permissible. This lesson clarifies which animals a muhrim may slaughter without incurring any penalty, based on the principle that only wild animals constitute sayd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states 'la ba'sa' (no harm), indicating permissibility. Determine the hukm level (mubah or ja'iz).
In Hanafi fiqh, 'la ba'sa' typically indicates permissibility.
2
List the permissible animals
The text explicitly mentions sheep, cow, camel, chicken, and domestic duck as permissible to slaughter.
The list is illustrative of domestic animals.
3
Understand the criterion
These animals are permissible because they are not game (sayd) due to lack of wildness (tawahhush).
The defining characteristic is whether the animal is wild by nature.
4
Analyze the duck specification
Only domestic duck that lives in houses and ponds is allowed; wild duck is prohibited because it is wild by nature.
The text clarifies that 'domestic duck' refers to those that are tame from origin.
5
Apply the principle
Any domestic animal not considered sayd is permissible; any wild animal is prohibited. This principle extends beyond the listed animals.
Apply the rule: if the animal is naturally wild, it is sayd; if domestic, it is not.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَا بَأسَ لِلمُحرم أن يَذْبَحَ الشَّاةَ وَالْبَقَرَة وَ الْبَعِيرَ وَالدَّجَاجَةَ وَالْبَطَ الْأهْلَى لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءَ لَيْسَتْ بِصُيُودٍ لِعَدَمِ التَّوَحُشِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْبَطِ الَّذِي يَكُونُ فِي الْمَسَاكِنِ وَالْحَيَاضِ لأنه الوف بأصلِ الْخِلْقَةِ
ترجمہ اور محرم کے لئے بکری ، گائے، اونٹ ، مرغی اور پالتو نخ کو ذبح کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ چیز میں وحشی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے صید نہیں ہیں اور بط سے مراد وہ بط ہے جو گھروں اور حوضوں میں رہتی ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل خلقت میں مانوس اور ہلی ہوئی ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And there is no harm for the muhrim to slaughter the sheep, the cow, the camel, the chicken, and the domestic duck, because these things are not game (sayd) due to lack of wildness. And what is meant by duck is that which lives in houses and ponds, because it is tame by original nature.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage clarifies which animals a muhrim may slaughter without incurring any penalty. The criterion is that the animal must be domestic (not wild) and thus not considered 'sayd' (game). The list includes sheep, cow, camel, chicken, and domestic duck. The commentator specifies that even among ducks, only domesticated ones are allowed, not wild ducks that are naturally wild. This ruling is straightforward: since these animals are not game, they are not subject to the hunting prohibition during ihram.

Key Terms
الصَّيْد (al-sayd): Wild game animals that are prohibited to hunt in ihram.
التَّوَحُش (al-tawahhush): Wildness or being untamed, the characteristic that makes an animal sayd.
الْبَطَّ الْأَهْلَى (al-batta al-ahliyya): Domestic duck that lives in houses and ponds, as opposed to wild duck.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A cow

Key Takeaway
A muhrim may slaughter any domestic animal that is not wild by nature; the key is distinguishing sayd (game) from non-sayd.

Ruling on Killing a Pamoz Pigeon in Ihram
Hanafi dispute with Malik on whether a pamoz pigeon counts as game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers the pamoz pigeon as wild game requiring compensation in ihram, and distinguish the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
A pigeon's original wild nature prevails over incidental domestication, so compensation is due.

This passage presents a disagreement between the Hanafi and Maliki schools regarding a specific type of pigeon known as the 'pamoz' (musarwal). While the Maliki school considers it domesticated due to its sluggish flight and tameness, the Hanafi school insists on its inherent wildness. Understanding this dispute reveals how each school weighs original attributes versus acquired characteristics. Let us dissect the arguments.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that compensation (jaza') is wajib for killing a pamoz pigeon in ihram.
The ruling is based on the pigeon's wild nature.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik considers the pamoz pigeon domesticated (musta'nas) and not wild game, so no compensation is owed.
Opponent's view: it is not sayd.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Maliki proof: the pigeon is slow to take off, lives around people, and is tame, making it domesticated.
The sluggish flight is cited as evidence of tameness.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Hanafi response: All pigeons are wild by original nature (mutawahhish bi-asl al-khilqah). Domestication is incidental and does not change this; the pigeon can still fly, even if slowly.
The Hanafi principle: original nature overrides incidental attributes.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Hanafi, the muhrim owes compensation; under Maliki, no compensation is owed.
This affects the muhrim's liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ ذَبَحَ حَمَامًا مُسْرُولًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاء خِلَافًا لِمَالِكِ لَهُ أَنَّهُ الَّوْقُ مُسْتَأْنَسٌ وَلَا يَمْتَنِعُ بِجَنَاحَيْهِ لِبُطُو نُهُوضِه وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ الْحَمامُ مَتَوَحِشُ بِأصْلِ الْخِلْقَةِ مُمْتَنِعُ بِطَيَرَانِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَ بَطِئَ النُّهُوضِ وَالِاسْتِينَاسُ عَارِضَ فَلَمْ يُعتبر
ترجمہ اور اگرمحرم نے پاموز کبوتر ذبح کیا تو اس پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پا موز کبوتر ہلا ہوا لوگوں سے مانوس ہوتا ہے اور اپنے بازو سے بچاؤ نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس کی اٹھان کے ست ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کبوتر اصل خلقت کے اعتبار سے وحشی ہوتا ہے جو کہ اپنی اڑان سے اپنا بچاؤ کرتا ہے اگر چہ انھان میں ست ہو اور مانوس ہونا عارض ہو گیا۔ لہذا اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح مسرول ، وہ کبوتر جس کے پاؤں میں بال و پر خوب ہوں گویا اس نے سراویل یعنی پانجامہ پہن رکھا ہے اس کو پاموز کہتے ہیں۔
And if he slaughters a pigeon with feathered feet (musarwal), then the compensation is upon him, contrary to Malik, because for him, it is a domesticated bird and it cannot protect itself with its wings due to the sluggishness of its rising. And we say: The pigeon is wild by original nature, preventing [capture] by its flight, even if it is slow in rising. And domestication is incidental, so it is not considered.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage deals with the status of a specific type of pigeon called 'pamoz' (musarwal), which has feathers covering its feet and is slow to take off. Imam Malik considers it domesticated (mustanis) because it lives around people and cannot easily escape, so it is not considered wild game. Thus, killing it in ihram would incur no penalty. The Hanafi position disagrees, arguing that all pigeons are inherently wild, capable of flight, even if this particular type is slow. Domestication is an incidental condition that does not change its fundamental nature as game. Therefore, killing it requires compensation (jaza'). The commentator explains that 'musarwal' literally means 'trousered', referring to the feathered feet resembling trousers.

Key Terms
حَمَامًا مُسْرُولًا (hamaman musarwalan): A pigeon with abundant feathers on its feet, also called 'pamoz' (fur-footed).
مُسْتَأْنَس (musta'nas): Domesticated or tame, accustomed to humans.
مَتَوَحِش (mutawahhish): Wild by original nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim kills a pamoz pigeon (musarwal), what is the ruling?
A) No compensation is required because it is domesticated
B) Compensation is required because it is still considered wild game
C) Only a small fine is required
D) He must free a slave

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires compensation for killing any pigeon in ihram, regardless of domestication, because its original wild nature prevails.

Penalty for a Muhrim Compelled to Kill Game
States ruling with Quranic proof that compulsion does not remove penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a muhrim compelled to kill game and explain the Quranic proof that ties permission to expiation.

Core Idea
Compulsion permits the act but does not remove the penalty—permission is conditional on expiation.

When a muhrim faces extreme hunger, Islam grants a concession to kill game, but this concession does not come free. The Hanafi school, relying on the Quranic principle that any permission for a prohibited act in ihram is tied to a compensatory penalty, rules that the jaza remains wajib. In this lesson, we will examine the proof and the underlying legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a muhrim compelled by necessity (e.g., extreme hunger) to kill game. The ruling is that the penalty (jaza) is wajib (obligatory).
The ruling holds even though the act itself becomes permissible due to necessity.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The proof is from Surah Al-Baqarah (2:196), which permits shaving the head during ihram due to illness but ties it to fidyah (expiation).
The verse is cited in the passage: فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنكُمْ مَرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ.
3
Trace the analogy (qiyas)
The verse establishes a principle: any permission for a prohibited act in ihram is conditional upon expiation. By applying this principle via qiyas, killing game under compulsion also requires expiation (the jaza).
This analogy is the core legal reasoning: the illah (effective cause) is the permission for a prohibited ihram act tied to compensation.
4
Confirm the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that necessity permits the act but does not eliminate the obligation of penalty. The permission (idhn) is muqayyad (conditional) with kaffarah.
The mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that the penalty is wajib even under compulsion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإنِ اضْطَرَّ الْمُحْرِمُ إلى قَتْل صَيْدٍ فَقَتَلَهُ فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاء لِأَنَّ الْإِذَنَ مُقَيَّدٌ بِالْكَفَّارَةِ بِالنَّصِّ عَلَى مَا تَلَوْنَاهُ مِنْ قَبْلُ ترجمہ اور اگر محرم کسی شکار کو قتل کرنے کے لئے مجبور ہو۔ پس اس نے اس کو قتل کر دیا تو اس پر جزاء واجب ہے کیونکہ اجازت نص کی وجہ سے کفارہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے چنانچہ ہم پہلے تلاوت کر چکے ہیں۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر محرم شدت بھوک وغیرہ کی وجہ سے شکار کو قتل کرنے کی طرف مضطر اور مجبور ہوا۔ چنانچہ اس نے شکار کو مار ڈالا تو اس پر بھی جزاء واجب ہے کیونکہ شریعت نے احرام کے ممنوعات میں سے اگر کسی ممنوع کام کو کرنے کی اجازت دی ہے تو وہ اجازت کفارہ کے ساتھ مقید ہے۔ چنانچہ باری تعالیٰ کا ارشاد ہے فَمَنْ كَانَ مِنكُمْ مَرِيضًا أَوْ بِهِ أَذًى مِنْ رَأْسِهِ فَفِدْيَةٌ مِنْ صِيَامٍ أَوْ صَدَقَةٍ أَوْ نُسُكٍ ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ اللہ تعالیٰ نے ضرورت کے وقت سر منڈانے کی اجازت دی ہے مگر فدیہ کفارہ کے ساتھ ۔ پس اسی طرح مضطر کو بھی ضرورت کے وقت شکار ذبح کر کے کھانا جائز ہے مگر بشرط کفارہ اور شکار کا کفارہ اس کی جزاء ہے جس کی تفصیل سابق میں گذر چکی۔
And if a muhrim is compelled to kill game and kills it, then upon him is the penalty, because permission is tied to expiation by the text as we have recited before. Translation: And if a muhrim is forced to kill game. Then he killed it, then upon him the penalty is obligatory, because permission due to the text is tied to expiation, as we have recited before. Commentary: The issue is that if a muhrim due to severe hunger etc. is forced and compelled to kill game, and he kills it, then upon him also the penalty is obligatory, because the Shariah has permitted, among the prohibitions of ihram, to do a prohibited act, then that permission is tied to expiation. Thus Allah's saying: 'So whoever among you is ill or has an ailment of the head, then a ransom of fasting or charity or sacrifice.' Observe that Allah permitted shaving the head at the time of necessity but with fidyah expiation. So similarly, the compelled one is also permitted to slaughter and eat game at the time of necessity but with the condition of expiation, and the expiation for game is its penalty, the detail of which has passed earlier.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling is that if a muhrim is compelled (mudtarr) by necessity such as extreme hunger to kill game, the penalty (jaza) is still wajib. The proof is from the Quranic verse (2:196) where permission to shave the head during ihram due to illness is explicitly tied to fidyah. By analogy, any permission granted for a prohibited act in ihram is conditional upon expiation. The Hanafi position is that necessity does not remove the obligation of penalty; it only permits the act. This is based on the principle that the original prohibition remains, and the concession is granted with a compensatory requirement. The passage emphasizes that the permission (idhn) is muqayyad (limited/conditional) with kaffarah. The commentary further explains that the Shariah's pattern is consistent: any dispensation from a prohibtion of ihram comes with a prescribed compensation. The detail of the specific penalties for various games is referenced as having passed earlier.

Key Terms
مضطر (mudtarr): One who is compelled by necessity, e.g., extreme hunger, to perform a prohibited act.
جزاء (jaza): The specific penalty for killing game while in ihram, varying by animal.
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation; the compensation required when a prohibited act is permitted due to necessity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible without any penalty
B) It is permissible but the penalty (jaza) is wajib
C) It is absolutely forbidden even if starving
D) It is permissible only if he gives charity

Key Takeaway
Even under compulsion, a muhrim who kills game must pay the penalty; permission is conditional upon expiation.

Animals a Muhrim May Slaughter
Ruling statement listing permissible domestic animals for a muhrim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the animals a muhrim may slaughter and explain the criterion of 'not being sayd' (wild game).

Core Idea
A muhrim may slaughter any domestic animal; only wild game is prohibited.

During ihram, hunting wild animals is forbidden. However, a pilgrim may still slaughter domestic animals for food. This passage from the Hanafi text clarifies exactly which animals are permissible, using the key criterion: the animal must not be 'sayd' (wild game). The list includes common livestock and poultry, with a specific note on domestic ducks.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The passage states 'la ba'sa' (no harm), indicating permissibility (mubah) for a muhrim to slaughter these animals.
This is a license, not an obligation.
2
List the permissible animals
Memorize the list: sheep (al-sha), cow (al-baqarah), camel (al-ba'eer), chicken (al-dajajah), and domesticated duck (al-batt al-ahli).
Notice the duck is qualified as 'ahli' (domestic).
3
Understand the criterion
The reason given: these are not sayd because they lack wildness (adam al-tawahhush). The underlying principle is that only wild game is prohibited for a muhrim to kill.
What defines 'wild'? The animal's original creation (asl al-khilqah) – if inherently tame, it is not sayd.
4
Apply the duck clarification
The text specifies that 'duck' means the one living in houses and basins, tame by original creation. This excludes wild ducks, which are considered game and thus haram to slaughter in ihram.
This shows that not all ducks are equal; species alone is not decisive – domesticity is key.

وَلَا بَأسَ لِلمُحرم أن يَذْبَحَ الشَّاةَ وَالْبَقَرَة وَ الْبَعِيرَ وَالدَّجَاجَةَ وَالْبَطَ الْأهْلَى لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاءَ لَيْسَتْ بِصُيُودٍ لِعَدَمِ التَّوَحُشِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْبَطِ الَّذِي يَكُونُ فِي الْمَسَاكِنِ وَالْحَيَاضِ لأنه الوف بأصلِ الْخِلْقَةِ ترجمہ اور محرم کے لئے بکری ، گائے، اونٹ ، مرغی اور پالتو نخ کو ذبح کرنے میں کوئی مضائقہ نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ چیز میں وحشی نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے صید نہیں ہیں اور بط سے مراد وہ بط ہے جو گھروں اور حوضوں میں رہتی ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل خلقت میں مانوس اور ہلی ہوئی ہے۔ تشریح واضح ہے۔
And there is no harm for a muhrim to slaughter a sheep, a cow, a camel, a chicken, and a domesticated duck, because these things are not game due to lack of wildness. And by 'duck' is meant the one that is in houses and basins, because it is tame by original creation. Translation: And for a muhrim, there is no harm in slaughtering a goat, cow, camel, chicken, and domesticated duck. Because these are not game due to being non-wild. And by 'duck' is meant the duck that lives in houses and basins because it is tame and domestic by original creation. Commentary: It is clear.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage is a simple ruling statement listing animals a muhrim may slaughter without penalty. The list includes sheep, cow, camel, chicken, and domesticated duck. The reasoning is that these are not considered 'sayd' (game) because they are not wild animals (mutawahhish). The specification of duck is clarified: it refers to ducks that live in domestic settings (houses and basins) as they are inherently tame (alf bi asl al-khilqah). Domestic ducks are not considered wild, even if they have some ability to fly. This ruling is straightforward and serves as a memorization anchor for the permissible slaughter animals during ihram.

Key Terms
صيد (sayd): Wild game animals that are prohibited to hunt or kill while in ihram.
البط الأهلي (al-batt al-ahli): Domesticated duck, raised in houses or basins, as opposed to wild ducks.

Ruling on Slaughtering a Musrūl (Feather-footed) Pigeon
Presents Hanafi vs Maliki dispute on whether a musrūl pigeon is considered game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers a musrūl pigeon as game and evaluate the Maliki counterargument based on the principle of al-'ibrah li al-asl.

Core Idea
A pigeon's original wildness determines its game status; accidental tameness does not change the ruling.

In ihram, slaughtering game incurs a penalty. But what if a pigeon appears tame? The Hanafi and Maliki schools differ. This passage explains why the Hanafi school insists on looking at the original nature, not temporary tameness.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the Hanafi ruling: slaughtering a musrūl pigeon by a muhrim requires the penalty (jaza). The basis is original wildness.
The pigeon is considered game (sayd) by default.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam Malik holds that no penalty is due because the pigeon is tame (musta'nis) and cannot defend itself due to slow rising.
Maliki focuses on observable behavior.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Maliki proof: the pigeon is familiar with people and slow to take flight, so it is not true game.
This is a valid ikhtilaf.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response invokes the principle: the pigeon is originally wild (asl al-khilqah) and defends itself by flight; tameness is accidental (arid) and does not change the ruling.
Al-'ibrah li al-asl: consideration is given to the original nature.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi imposes penalty, Maliki does not.
This affects a muhrim's liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ ذَبَحَ حَمَامًا مُسْرُولًا فَعَلَيْهِ الْجَزَاء خِلَافًا لِمَالِكِ لَهُ أَنَّهُ الْوَقْ مُستَانِسٌ وَلَا يَمْسِيعُ بِجَنَاحَيْهِ لِبُطُو نُهُوضِه وَنَحْنُ نَقُولُ الْحَمامُ مَتَوَحِشُ بِأصْلِ الْخِلْقَةِ مُمتِنُعِ بِطِيرَ إِنه وَإِنْ كَانَ بَطِئَ النُّهُوضِ وَالْاسْتَيَنَاسُ عَارِضَ فَلَمْ يُعْتَبَرْ ترجمہ اور اگر محرم نے پاموز کبوتر ذبح کیا تو اس پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ امام مالک کا اختلاف ہے۔ امام مالک کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ پا موز کبوتر ہلا ہوا لوگوں سے مانوس ہوتا ہے اور اپنے بازو سے بچاؤ نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس کی اٹھان کے ست ہونے کی وجہ سے اور ہم کہتے ہیں کہ کبوتر اصل خلقت کے اعتبار سے وحشی ہوتا ہے جو کہ اپنی اڑان سے اپنا بچاؤ کرتا ہے اگر چہ انھان میں ست ہو اور مانوس ہونا عارض ہو گیا۔ لہذا اس کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح مسرول ، وہ کبوتر جس کے پاؤں میں بال و پر خوب ہوں گویا اس نے سراویل یعنی پانجامہ پہن رکھا ہے اس کو پاموز کہتے ہیں۔
And if he slaughtered a musrūl pigeon, then upon him is the penalty, contrary to Malik, because [for Malik] it is tame and does not defend itself with its wings due to sluggishness in rising. And we say: the pigeon is wild by original creation, defending itself by flight, even if it is slow in rising, and tameness is accidental, so it is not considered. Translation: And if a muhrim slaughtered a pa-moz pigeon, then upon him the penalty is wajib. Imam Malik disagreed. Imam Malik's proof is that the pa-moz pigeon is tame, familiar with people, and cannot defend itself with its wings due to its slow rising. And we say: the pigeon is by original creation wild, defending itself by its flight, even if its rising is slow, and tameness is accidental. Therefore it will not be considered. Commentary: Musrūl is a pigeon whose feet have abundant feathers, as if it is wearing trousers, called pa-moz.
Source pages p. 469

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi-Maliki dispute on whether a musrūl pigeon (a pigeon with feathered feet, also called pa-moz) is considered game (sayd). The Hanafi position is that slaughtering it incurs the penalty (jaza). Malik holds that no penalty is due because the pigeon is domesticated (musta'nis) and cannot properly fly or defend itself. The Hanafi response: pigeons are originally wild (mutawahhish bi asl al-khilqah) and can defend themselves by flight, even if sluggish. Tameness is a temporary accidental state (arid) and does not change the essential nature. In Hanafi fiqh, legal consideration ('itibar) is given to the original state not the accidental one (al-'ibrah li al-asl). Thus the musrūl pigeon retains the ruling of game. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that transformative attributes (like tameness) must be stable and not merely accidental to affect the ruling.

Key Terms
مسرول (musrūl): A pigeon with feathers on its feet, resembling trousers (pa-moz).
عارض (arid): Accidental or temporary state that does not change the essential nature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it is originally wild and tameness is accidental
C) Because it has feathers on its feet
D) Because Imam Malik said so

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a musrūl pigeon is considered game based on its original wildness; accidental tameness does not affect the ruling.

The Ruling on Slaughtering a Tame Deer (Qiyas on Original Wildness)
Extends the ruling to tame deer via qiyas and contrasts with camel

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that tameness does not remove the ruling of game for originally wild animals, using qiyas jali.

Core Idea
Original wildness (asl al-khilqah) is decisive; tameness is accidental and does not change the ruling.

In this passage, al-Marghinani addresses a subtle question: if a deer becomes tame, does it cease to be 'game' (sayd) for the muhrim? The answer uses qiyas (analogy) to established rulings and a contrast with a camel to clarify the principle. Understanding this helps you grasp how the Hanafi school treats accidental changes while preserving original legal categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the far' (new case)
The passage extends a prior ruling to a tame deer. What is the new case being judged? Recognize: a tame deer (zaby musta'nis).
The prior ruling was for a tame pigeon (musrūl).
2
Extract the illa (effective cause)
Find the common attribute that justifies analogizing the deer to the pigeon. The text says: 'because it is game in origin' (sayd fi al-asl). That is the illa.
The illa is the original wild nature, not the current tameness.
3
Apply the qiyas to derive the ruling
Since the illa exists in both, the ruling transfers: killing a tame deer incurs the same penalty as killing a tame pigeon.
The ruling is wajib penalty.
4
Contrast with the camel example
The camel is originally domestic; even if it becomes wild temporarily, it does not take the ruling of game. This confirms the principle by showing the opposite scenario.
This is a counter-analogy (tamthil bi al-muqabil) to reinforce the illa.
5
State the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position is that the penalty is wajib for a muhrim who kills a tame deer. This is from Zahir al-Riwayah.
The position is mukhtalaf fih – other schools may differ, but the Hanafi view is as stated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَا إِذَا قَتَلَ طَيْنَا مُسْتَأْنِسًا لِأَنَّهُ صَيْدُ فِي الْأَصْلِ فَلَا يُبْطِلُهُ الْإِسْتِيْنَاسُ كَالْبَعِيرِ إِذَا يَدَلَا يَأْخُذُحُكْمَ الصَّيْدِ فِي الْحُرُمَةِ عَلَى الْمُحَرِمِ ترجمہ اور یوں ہی جب ہلی ہوئی ہرن کو ذبح کیا تو جزاء واجب ہے کیونکہ وہ اصل میں صید ہے تو اس کو ہلا ہوا ہونا باطل نہیں کرے گا۔ جیسے اونٹ جبکہ بھڑک کر وحشت کھا گیا تو وہ صید کا حکم نہیں لیتا کہ محرم پر اس کا ذبح کرنا حرام ہو جاوے۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کسی بلی ہوئی ہرن کو قتل کر دیا تو محرم پر جزاء واجب ہے۔ کیونکہ ہرن اصل خلقت کے اعتبار سے صید ہے اور اول کا ہلا ہوا ہونا اس کو عارض ہوا ہے اس لئے ہلا ہوا ہونا اس کے صید ہونے کو باطل نہیں کرے گا جیسے ایک اونٹ ایک اہلی اور پالتو جانور ہے لیکن اگر وہ لوگوں سے بدک کر وحشت کھانے لگا تو وہ اہلی ہونے سے نہیں نکلے گا اور محرم پر حرام ہونے میں شکار کا حکم نہیں لے گا۔
And likewise, if he killed a tame deer, because it is game in origin, so tameness does not nullify it. Like the camel which, if it becomes wild, does not take the ruling of game in prohibition upon the muhrim. Translation: And similarly, when a tame deer is slaughtered, the penalty is wajib, because it is game in origin, so its being tame does not nullify it. Like a camel when it starts to become wild, it does not take the ruling of game that it becomes prohibited for a muhrim to slaughter. Commentary: The issue: if a muhrim kills a tame deer, the penalty is wajib. Because the deer is by original creation game, and its being tame is accidental. So tameness does not nullify its being game. Just like a camel is a domestic animal, but if it becomes wild due to fleeing from people, it does not leave its domestic status and does not take the ruling of game for the muhrim's prohibition.
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage uses qiyas (analogy) to establish the ruling for a tame deer. The asl (original case) is the musrūl pigeon from the previous discussion: a pigeon is originally wild, so tameness does not change its status as game. The far' (new case) is a tame deer: it is originally wild, so tameness is accidental and does not nullify its game status. The illa (effective cause) is that the animal is originally wild (sayd fi al-asl). The ruling for the far' is that killing it incurs the penalty. The passage also draws a contrast with a camel: a camel is originally domestic, so if it becomes wild temporarily, it does not become game—meaning a muhrim can still slaughter it without penalty. This illustrates the Hanafi principle of considering the original state (asl) over the accidental (arid). The camel example is a counter-analogy to show that tameness does not make a wild animal domestic, nor does wildness make a domestic animal wild.

Key Terms
مستأنس (musta'nis): Tame, domesticated, accustomed to humans.
صيد في الأصل (sayd fi al-asl): Originally game; an animal that is wild by its original creation.
عارض ('arid): Accidental, temporary attribute that does not change the essence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) No penalty because it is tame
B) Penalty is wajib because it is originally game
C) It is halal to eat without penalty
D) The muhrim must sacrifice a camel instead

Key Takeaway
Original wildness determines the ruling; tameness is accidental and does not remove the status of game.

The Muhrim's Slaughter: Carrion or Halal?
Hanafi vs Shafi'i dispute on muhrim's slaughter validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on a muhrim's slaughter, identify the Shafi'i counter-argument, and explain the Hanafi response using the analogy to the Magian's slaughter.

Core Idea
A muhrim's slaughter is invalid because a forbidden act cannot be a prescribed slaughter—like the Magian's.

This lesson examines a classic dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: if a person in ihram (muhrim) slaughters game, is the meat halal for a non-muhrim? The Hanafi school rules that the slaughter is invalid and the animal is carrion, while Imam al-Shafi'i allows it when the muhrim acts as an agent. We will explore the proofs on both sides and understand the underlying principle that the validity of slaughter depends on the act being prescribed (mashru').

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: a muhrim's slaughter is invalid, the meat is carrion (maytah) and not halal for anyone.
This is absolute; agency does not change the ruling.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that if the muhrim slaughters for a non-muhrim, the meat is halal for that non-muhrim because the muhrim is an agent.
The act is attributed to the principal.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Shafi'i proof is based on agency: the muhrim's act is transferred to the principal, so the forbiddenness does not affect the principal.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response: validity of slaughter depends on the act being prescribed (mashru') itself; a forbidden act cannot be a valid means of slaughter regardless of who benefits. They use qiyas to the slaughter of a Magian.
Magian's slaughter is invalid because the act is not sanctioned.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafi says meat is haram for all; Shafi'i says halal for the non-muhrim principal.
This affects actual consumption.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِذَا ذَبَحَ الْمُحْرِمُ صَيْدًا فَذَبِيحَتُهُ مَيْتَةٌ لَا يَحِلُّ أُكُلُهَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَحِلُّ مِمَّا ذَبَحَهُ الْمُحْرِمُ لِغَيْرِهِ لِأَنَّهُ عَامِلَ فَانْتَقَلَ لَهُ فِعَلَهُ إِلَيْهِ وَلَنَا أَنَّ الزَّكَاةَ فِعْلٌ مَشْرُوعٌ وَهَذَا فِعْلٌ حَرَامٌ فَلَا يَكُونُ ذَكَاةً كَذَبِيحَةِ الْمُجُوسِى وَهَذَا لأنَّ الْمَشْرُوعَ هُوَ الَّذِى قَامَ مَقَامَ الْمَيْزِ بَيْنَ الدَّم وَاللَّحْم تَيْسِرًا فَيَنْعَدِمُ بِالعَدَامِهِ ا ترجمہ اور جب محرم نے کسی شکار کو ذبح کیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ مردار ہے اس کا کھانا حلال نہیں ہے۔ اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ جس کو محرم نے ذبح کیا وہ غیر محرم کے لئے حلال ہے کیونکہ محرم دوسرے کے لئے کام کرنے والا ہے۔ پس اس کا فعل دوسرے کی طرف منتقل ہو گا اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ذبح کرنا مشروع فعل ہے اور محرم کا یہ فعل حرام ہے تو یہ ذبح کرنا نہ ہو گا۔ جیسے آتش پرست کا ذبیحہ۔ اور یہ اس وجہ سے ہے کہ ذبح مشروع وہی آسانی کے واسطے خون اور گوشت کے درمیان جدائی کرنے کے قائم مقام ہے۔ پس حلال ہونا معدوم ہو گا ذبح مشروع معدوم ہونے کی وجہ سے ۔ تشریح مسئلہ، اگر محرم نے کسی شکار کو ذبح کیا تو اس کا ذبیحہ مردار ہے اس کا کھانا کسی کے لئے حلال نہیں ہے۔ امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ
And when a muhrim slaughters game, his slaughtered animal is carrion; its consumption is not permissible. And al-Shafi'i said: that which the muhrim slaughters for another is halal, because he is an agent, so his action transfers to him. And our proof is that slaughter (zakah) is a prescribed act, and this is a forbidden act, so it is not valid slaughter, like the slaughter of a Magian. And this is because the prescribed act is that which stands in place of separating blood and flesh with ease, so it becomes nonexistent with its nonexistence. Translation: And when a muhrim slaughters any game, his slaughtered animal is carrion; eating it is not halal. Imam Shafi'i said that what a muhrim slaughters for another person is halal, because the muhrim is an agent for that person, so his action is transferred to that person. And our proof is that slaughter is a prescribed act (mashru'), and this act of the muhrim is forbidden, so it is not valid slaughter, like the slaughter of a fire-worshipper. And this is because the prescribed slaughter is that which serves to separate blood and flesh for ease, so halal status is absent due to the absence of prescribed slaughter. Commentary: The issue: if a muhrim slaughters game, his slaughter is carrion; its consumption is not halal for anyone. Imam Shafi'i says...
Source pages p. 470

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between Hanafi and Shafi'i on the validity of a muhrim's slaughter of game. The Hanafi position: the slaughter is invalid; the animal is carrion (maytah) and not halal for anyone, including non-muhrims. The Shafi'i position: if the muhrim slaughters for another person (non-muhrim), it is halal for that person because the muhrim acts as an agent (aamil) and the act is attributed to the principal. The Hanafi proof: zakah (ritual slaughter) is a prescribed act (mashru'), but the muhrim's act is forbidden (haram). A forbidden act cannot fulfill a prescribed requirement. The analogy (qiyas) is to the slaughter of a Magian (majusi), which is invalid and carrion even if done with proper method, because the act is not sanctioned. The underlying principle: the validity of slaughter depends on the act being lawful (mashru'); when the act is forbidden, the legal separation of blood and flesh is not achieved, so the meat is not halal. The Hanafi school considers the muhrim's violation of ihram as a prevention (mani') that invalidates the slaughter, regardless of intent or agency.

Key Terms
ذَكَاة (zakah): Ritual slaughter that makes an animal halal by cutting the throat in the prescribed manner.
ميتة (maytah): Carrion; meat from an animal that died without proper lawful slaughter.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim slaughters a deer for a non-muhrim, what is the ruling on the meat?
A) Halal for the non-muhrim
B) Carrion and not halal for anyone
C) Halal only if the muhrim did it unintentionally
D) Halal for the muhrim himself

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a muhrim's slaughter is invalid because the act is forbidden, and the animal is carrion for all.
